=== SESSION 34 ===
Date: 2026-05-30
Feature completed: SRS-MD-001 SDK-SURFACE — consolidated market-data
subscription dedup + fan-out for the "consolidate duplicate real-time
market data subscriptions across active strategies" requirement per
docs/SRS.md row SRS-MD-001 (traces SyRS SYS-70; StRS SN-1.10, SN-1.29,
SC-25, A-13). This is the *consolidation + fan-out* half of SYS-70; the
line-limit half is SRS-MD-002 (subscription_limit_contract), already
shipped. The new Rust surface is ConsolidatedSubscriptionRegistry in
crates/atp-market-data: it owns the live subscription set and enforces
the SRS-MD-001 invariant — exactly ONE upstream IB subscription per
distinct security regardless of how many strategy containers subscribe;
fan_out routes a received MarketDataTick to every subscriber of its
symbol and to NO other subscriber. It publishes a SubscriptionChange-
Event (the SyRS SYS-61 / SRS-LOG-001 subscription_change event for
Source.MARKET_DATA) on every line-affecting / dedup transition through a
SubscriptionChangeSink port, fails closed (SubscriptionRegistryError)
on empty symbol / strategy id, and — the cross-feature seam — IS the
concrete SubscriptionLineCounter the SRS-MD-002 gate consumes, closing
subscription_limit_contract.deferred[]'s "owner: SRS-MD-001" item
(try_acquire is dedup-aware: a duplicate of an already-subscribed
security consumes no new line). New shared types live in
crates/atp-types (MarketDataTick, SubscriptionChange,
SubscriptionChangeEvent). The contract is pinned in
architecture/runtime_services.json#subscription_fanout_contract and
enforced by tools/subscription_fanout_check.py (10 static evidence
collectors + cargo smoke) + tests/test_subscription_fanout_contract.py
L3 mutation suite + tests/domain/test_subscription_fanout_dedup.py L7
runner over crates/atp-market-data/tests/srs_md_001_subscription_fanout.rs.
Status: 92 remaining features (unchanged — SRS-MD-001 stays passes:false
per the SDK-surface partial-pass pattern; the AC's <=100 ms fan-out
latency NFR + the real IB feed + the async fan-out transport are the
deferred runtime halves).

Feature pick: surfaced the choice to the user via AskUserQuestion
(SRS-MD-001 SDK-surface vs SRS-NOTIF-001 SDK-surface vs a CI-mirror
cleanup chore). User chose SRS-MD-001 SDK-surface at the established
smallest-blast-radius depth. Correction to SESSION 33's handoff:
SRS-SDK-007 is actually P2 (bar consolidation/resampling), not a
strategy-side logging API, so it was out of priority order; the two
genuine next-honest P1 candidates were SRS-MD-001 (lower ID, top
recommendation) and SRS-NOTIF-001.

Carryover audit at session start: SESSION 33's recommendation that
SRS-MD-001 was a clean next P1 was sound. Phase-1 exploration confirmed
the seam was already half-modeled in Rust: crates/atp-market-data
already had MarketDataSubscriptionManager with owns_subscription_fanout()
-> true but NO actual fan-out, and a SubscriptionLineCounter trait whose
deferred[] (in subscription_limit_contract) explicitly names SRS-MD-001
as the owner of "the live subscription set". So SRS-MD-001's honest home
is RUST extending crates/atp-market-data (AC-16: the subscription
manager is a core Rust runtime service) — NOT a python/atp_* SDK package
like the recent LOG-001/API-001/ERR-9 sessions (those are Python
Strategy-API / cross-cutting surfaces). Closest template was
SRS-MD-002 / subscription_limit_check.py (same crate, same Rust static-
check style via tools/_rust_parser.py + a cargo smoke step).

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- SRS-MD-001 stays passes:false. The runtime consumers required for
  end-to-end verification are in
  architecture/runtime_services.json#subscription_fanout_contract.deferred[]:
    (1) SRS-MD-001-runtime — real IB reqMktData/cancelMktData binding
        driven by the registry's Opened/Closed transitions, live tick
        ingestion, the async fan-out transport, and thread-safe
        concurrency (the registry is single-threaded by design);
    (2) SRS-PERF-001 — the <=100 ms fan-out latency NFR measured against
        a PTP-disciplined clock (the deferred performance half, same
        pattern as SRS-SDK-004's deferred p95);
    (3) SRS-EXE-006 — the headless IB Gateway adapter owning the actual
        market-data API calls;
    (4) SRS-MD-003 / SRS-MD-007 — heartbeat freshness + tick sequence-gap
        detection that mark a consolidated subscription stale
        (tick_seq is the opaque hook; gap semantics are MD-007's);
    (5) SRS-LOG-001-runtime — the persistent sink for the
        subscription_change events (Source.MARKET_DATA);
    (6) SRS-UI-001 / SRS-API-001 — dashboard line-usage pane + REST/WS
        surfacing of lines_in_use / subscriber_count + operator alerts.
  SRS-MD-001 can flip passes:true when the SRS-MD-001-runtime fan-out
  transport + SRS-PERF-001 latency evidence land.

- IMPORTANT — pre-existing workspace toolchain drift discovered this
  session (NOT introduced by this diff; deferred, mirrors the long-
  standing deferred-ruff note): the locally-installed Rust toolchain
  (rust-1.95.0 clippy/rustfmt) is NEWER than whatever last linted the
  repo and surfaces lints across MANY pre-existing files:
    * `cargo fmt --check` flags 13 pre-existing files (atp-data/src +
      its err_5/err_6 tests, atp-execution/src + err_2 test,
      atp-market-data/src + err_4 test, atp-orchestrator/src + its 4
      orch_* tests, atp-types/src) — ALL drift at pure HEAD too.
    * `cargo clippy --workspace` has ~4-5 pre-existing errors in
      atp-orchestrator (large-Err-variant, too-many-arguments,
      sort_by_key) — present at HEAD.
  TRAP for the next agent: do NOT run `cargo fmt` (whole-crate) as part
  of a feature — it reformats pre-existing single-line enum struct-
  variants (e.g. `MemBelowFloor { mem_mb: u32, floor_mb: u32 },`) into
  multi-line, which (a) is unrelated churn and (b) BREAKS the orchestrator
  / MD-002 L3 contract tests that do literal `.replace()` on the Rust
  source (test_orchestrator_resource_profile_contract / _lifecycle).
  This session hit exactly that, reverted, and re-applied additions via
  Edit so pre-existing lines stayed byte-identical. Hand-format new lines
  to match the COMMITTED style instead. A future `chore(fmt): re-run
  rustfmt across the workspace` would need to ALSO update the literal-
  replace strings in the affected L3 tests in the same commit.

- Pre-existing ci.yml <-> run_ci_locally.sh mirror drift persists (the
  7 strategy_api_* checks still missing from run_ci_locally.sh, same as
  SESSION 31-33). subscription_fanout_check.py is a cargo-based check,
  so — like its sibling subscription_limit_check.py — it is intentionally
  NOT in either loop; its static evidence runs in CI via the L3 pytest
  contract test and its Rust behavior via `cargo test --workspace`.
  A future `chore(ci): re-sync run_ci_locally.sh with ci.yml` should add
  the 7 missing python-loop checks in one batch.

  (kill switch + IB adapter). The next honest P1 SDK-surface candidate

=== SESSION 33 ===
Date: 2026-05-22
Feature completed: SRS-LOG-001 SDK-SURFACE — log record schema +
sink-routing boundary for the system-level "separate persistent system
logs from user strategy logs; render each entry with timestamp /
severity / source / event type / message / correlation ID; both
classes viewable from the dashboard" requirement per docs/SRS.md row
SRS-LOG-001 (traces SyRS SYS-38 + SYS-61; StRS SN-2.02, C-6). The SDK
now ships a python/atp_logging/ package — LogRecord frozen dataclass
with the 8 contracted fields, AC-pinned StrEnums Severity (DEBUG /
INFO / WARN / ERROR / CRITICAL verbatim from SYS-61), LogClass (SYSTEM
/ STRATEGY — the SRS-LOG-001 separation discriminant), Source (8
SYSTEM emitter components from SYS-61 + 1 STRATEGY), EVENT_TYPES_BY_
SOURCE map pinning the 17 AC-named system event types, RoutedLog-
Dispatcher that validates every record at the dispatch boundary +
routes on log_class so SYSTEM and STRATEGY land in separate persistent
sinks, LogSink Protocol the downstream sinks plug into, and a LogRecord
Error family (LogPayloadError / LogClassError / LogRoutingError /
LogSinkError) so callers catch the boundary with one except clause.
The cross-language contract is pinned in
architecture/runtime_services.json#log_record_contract and enforced by
tools/log_record_check.py (31 evidence collectors) +
tests/test_log_record_contract.py L3 mutation suite +
tests/domain/test_log_record_dispatch.py L7 reference-dispatcher
end-to-end runner.
Status: 92 remaining features (unchanged — SRS-LOG-001 stays
passes:false per the SDK-004 / SDK-005 / ERR-9 / SRS-API-001 SDK-
surface partial-pass pattern; see "What I tested" for the precise
scope and "Known issues / notes for next agent" for the deferred[]
audit).

Carryover audit at session start: SESSION 32's "The next honest P1 to
attempt would be SRS-LOG-001 (SDK-surface candidate: define the
LogRecord schema, severity/source/event-type enums, correlation-ID
propagation, and the persistent-sink boundary — the contract hooks
already exist via the as_log_records callout in the ERR-9 contract
block + the /api/v1/logs REST route + LOGS WS channel + `admin logs`
CLI command pinned by this session's contract)" was sound. Phase-1
exploration confirmed:
  * python/atp_api/routes.py declares GET /api/v1/logs with
    request_fields (log_class, severity, source, event_type,
    correlation_id, start_time, end_time) and response_fields
    (events, timestamp, severity, source, event_type, message,
    correlation_id);
  * python/atp_ws/channels.py declares the LOGS WebSocket channel
    with payload_fields (timestamp, severity, source, event_type,
    message, correlation_id);
  * python/atp_cli/commands.py declares the `admin logs` command
    with arguments (--log-class, --severity, --source, --since,
    --follow, --json);
  * the SRS AC + SyRS SYS-61 verbatim enumerate the 5 severity
    levels, 8 system-log emitter sources, and 17 event types per
    source — all AC-pinnable;
  * no python/atp_logging/ existed yet — clean slate for the SDK
    surface.
Surfaced two choices to the user via AskUserQuestion: (1) feature pick
(SRS-LOG-001 SDK-surface vs CI re-sync chore vs SRS-MD-001 SDK-surface
vs ERR-7/8 attempt), (2) contract depth (schema + enums + sink boundary
vs add correlation-ID contextvars vs full SDK + dashboard payload
renderers). User chose "SRS-LOG-001 SDK-surface" + "Schema + enums +
sink boundary" — the smallest blast radius matching SESSION 32's mode
(deferred correlation-ID context, dashboard renderers, and the runtime
sinks all stay deferred[]).

  Test classes:

Feature completed: SRS-API-001 SDK-SURFACE — operator workflow
coverage contract for the system-level "expose dashboard, CLI, and
REST/WebSocket interfaces for operator workflows" requirement per
docs/SRS.md row SRS-API-001 (traces SRS-5.8 SRS-API-001 + §7 rows
API-2 / API-3 / API-4; SyRS IF-8, IF-9, SYS-2c, SYS-44a, SYS-48,
SYS-49a; StRS SN-1.11, SN-1.25). The three per-surface contracts
(rest_api / cli / websocket_api) already verify each surface in
isolation; this session adds the cross-surface AC-coverage binding
that ties REST Capability + CLI Group + (optional) WebSocket Channel
buckets to the 8 operator workflows the AC enumerates verbatim —
"Live designation, strategy management, kill switch, Hot-Swap,
Reservoir ranking, backtests, system status, and logs" — so a CLI
group rename, a REST route deletion, or a Capability / Group / Channel
bucket renaming cannot silently drop an operator workflow. The
cross-surface contract is pinned in architecture/runtime_services.json
#operator_workflow_surface_contract and enforced by
tools/operator_workflow_surface_check.py (20 evidence collectors) +
tests/test_operator_workflow_surface_contract.py L3 mutation suite +
tests/domain/test_operator_workflow_surface.py L7 reference-operator-
client end-to-end runner.

passes:false per the SDK-surface partial-pass pattern; see "What I
tested" for the precise scope and "Known issues / notes for next
agent" for the deferred[] audit).

  clarifying the docstring + rewriting sma_crossover to use the
  direct-callback path; (2) Indicator Protocol docstring used
  a deep-path import + the new check did not scan docstring or
  README code fences — fixed by switching the import to the
  facade and adding check_docstring_code_fences_use_facade +
  check_readme_code_fences_use_facade; (3) L7 coverage was
  hardcoded to subscribe/order/log — fixed by driving from the
  contract block's required_strategy_context_methods and
  extending sma_crossover to demonstrate cancel + get_state /
  set_state; (4) README on_schedule row still said "tag you
  registered" — fixed plus added a ReadmeScheduleTagWordingTest
  positive-evidence assertion; (5) docstring fence extractor
  flattened continuation indentation and silently skipped
  SyntaxErrors — fixed by preserving the `>>>` /  `...` indent and
  failing closed on parse errors; the markdown extractor regex
  was tightened to require an explicit python / py language tag;
  (6) InMemoryScheduler docstring used a python.atp_strategy.
  calendar repo-layout import — fixed plus extended
  FORBIDDEN_INTERNAL_PREFIXES to cover the python.atp_strategy
  subtree; (7) the example scanner had its own narrow local
  forbidden-prefix tuple — fixed by sharing the global
  constant; (8) the example scanner didn't normalize relative
  imports — `from ..api import X` slipped through; fixed by
  adding _resolve_relative_import; (9) a bare relative-alias
  `from .. import api` slipped through because the scanner only
  validated the base path — fixed by also validating each alias
  against <resolved_base>.<alias.name>. Each round added at
  least one new L3 mutation test pinning the regression.

  `warm[_-]?up[_-]?replay`, `warmup[_-]?controller`,

  `indicator[_-]?initialization`, `historical[_-]?replay`
  tokens. Mirrors the SESSION 16-27 per-feature prep precedent.

- Feat commit (76c0f00, +1786 / -5, 10 files): shipped the
  warm-up SDK surface. New python/atp_strategy/warmup.py
  exposes WarmupState (PENDING / IN_PROGRESS / COMPLETE),
  WarmupController (state / warmup_bars / bars_replayed /
  symbols_replayed properties, run() method), and
  assert_warmup_complete(state) guard. The controller pulls
  warmup_bars historical bars per subscribed symbol, replays
  them through Strategy.on_bar in order, transitions to
  COMPLETE, then fires on_warmup_complete exactly once.

  Critical safety property the first /codex:adversarial-review
  pass surfaced (and the second pass approved after the fix):
  the controller is fail-closed on a short historical replay.
  If HistoricalData.get_bars returns fewer than warmup_bars
  bars for any subscribed symbol the controller raises
  WarmupNotComplete with a "short by N bars" message, leaves
  WarmupState at IN_PROGRESS, does NOT fire on_warmup_complete,
  and keeps assert_warmup_complete closed. Production
  dispatchers must halt the container and surface the failure
  to the operator rather than enter live trading with an
  unready indicator (a 200-period SMA needs at least 200 bars
  to become ready).

  Architecture metadata block strategy_api_warmup_contract is
  the cross-language source of truth: state members, canonical
  200-bar warm-up, helper functions, exports, docstring tokens,
  AC traces, deferred dispatcher ownership, and the explicit
  fail-closed history-shortfall behaviour Rust core dispatchers
  re-implement locally per AGENTS.md dependency direction (no
  Rust -> Python SDK dependency).

  Contract evidence script tools/strategy_api_warmup_check.py
  + wiring in tools/architecture_check.py + init.sh.

  L7 domain test tests/domain/test_warmup_replay.py: reference
  _RefDispatcher exercises the AC end-to-end with 200 historical
  bars + SMA(200), executable-bar / order-submission gating
  during warm-up, on_warmup_complete fires-exactly-once at the
  boundary, live/paper parity (same surface), NFR-R3 restart
  re-execution, short-history fail-closed cases (single + multi-
  subscription), and the zero-warmup degenerate path. 13 tests.

  L3 contract tests/test_strategy_api_warmup_contract.py:
  subprocess positive-evidence check + mutation rig that locks
  WarmupState members, controller method/property shape, the
  on_warmup_complete signature + docstring tokens, the short-
  history shortfall guard, the assert_warmup_complete body, and
  the package-level exports. 15 tests.

  enforces (1) payload-shape (rejects None, dict, schema-drifted
  payloads with a structured error), (2) event-type discriminant
  (rejects bare-string / unknown / non-enum event_type), (3)
  runtime type + finite validation (str identifiers; finite int/
  float fill_price + commission; non-negative int fill_quantity +
  cumulative_filled + remaining_quantity), (4) AC-named-four
  field-presence (FILL/PARTIAL_FILL/CANCELLED/REJECTED must carry
  fill_price/fill_quantity/commission), (5) sign discipline
  (fill_price never negative; FILL/PARTIAL_FILL require strictly
  positive fill_price + fill_quantity), (6) lifecycle consistency
  (FILL.remaining_quantity == 0; PARTIAL_FILL.remaining_quantity
  > 0; CANCELLED/REJECTED.fill_quantity == cumulative_filled), (7)
  terminal reason on CANCELLED/REJECTED/EXPIRED. Latency budgets
  exposed as LIVE_/PAPER_CALLBACK_LATENCY_P95_MS — the Python-
  side view of the cross-language source of truth in
  architecture/runtime_services.json (Rust core dispatchers read
  the metadata directly per AGENTS.md dependency direction; the
  contract check enforces parity).

- This SESSION 27 chore commit: appends this entry to
  progress.txt. feature_list.json is NOT modified — SRS-SDK-004
  stays passes:false.

- L3 mutation rig sys.modules side effect: any future L1 test
  that does a fresh ``import atp_strategy`` inside a test body
  (not at module level) will silently get the last L3 tmpdir's
  mutated module after teardown. The contract-check tool's
  ``_load_sdk_module`` does not restore sys.modules on close.
  Two safe patterns: (a) module-level imports only in L1 tests
  (current convention; both test_scheduler.py and the new
  test_asset_class_guard.py follow this); (b) harden
  ``_load_sdk_module`` and the L3 _MutationRig to track and
  restore the original sys.modules['atp_strategy'] entry on
  close. (a) is the established repo convention; (b) is a
  defensive hardening that could ship alongside whatever feature
  next touches the scheduler or subscriptions check tools.

=== SESSION 25 ===
Date: 2026-05-18
Feature completed: SRS-SDK-002 — trading-calendar-aware scheduling
primitives. The Python Strategy SDK now ships real NYSE / NASDAQ /
CBOE-aliased calendar resolution backed by exchange_calendars: NYSE
2026 holidays and early closes, DST spring-forward (2026-03-08) and
fall-back (2026-11-01) wall-clock preservation, 04:00–20:00 ET pre-
market and after-hours session boundaries, and a concrete
InMemoryScheduler resolving the four Scheduler Protocol methods
(at_market_open, at_market_close, every_n_minutes, cron) against the
calendar. Calendar horizon pinned to [2000-01-01, 2035-12-31] for
date-deterministic resolution; cron preserves wall-clock across DST
by localizing via pytz internally; cron registration uses a fixed
sentinel (no host-clock read); every_n_minutes snaps post-close
candidates to the next session open; offset and cron candidates are
validated against the [04:00, 20:00] ET window; cross-scheduler
handles are rejected by scheduler-identity check. NotATradingSession
and CalendarHorizonExceeded surface programming errors / stale-data
conditions cleanly. SyRS AC: SYS-6 + SYS-50 + SYS-51.
Status: 96 remaining features

  - Added `python/atp_strategy/calendar.py` (~220 lines):
    UsEquityTradingCalendar(frozen-slot dataclass) implementing
    TradingCalendar Protocol. for_exchange("NYSE" | "NASDAQ" | "CBOE")
    factory; CBOE aliased to XNYS (see Override below);

  - Added `python/atp_strategy/scheduler.py` (~370 lines):
    InMemoryScheduler(dataclass) implementing the four Scheduler
    Protocol methods. _CronAdapter wraps croniter — localizes base via
    pytz so wall-clock time is preserved across DST (zoneinfo + croniter
    drifts), then converts results back to zoneinfo on return. cron()
    validates syntax against a fixed sentinel `2000-01-01T12:00`
    (no datetime.now() — deterministic-time rule). next_fire_time
    rejects cross-scheduler handles by checking handle.scheduler is
    self. _resolve_market_open/close validate offset-derived fire is
    inside [premarket_open, afterhours_close] of the same session.
    _resolve_every_n snaps post-close candidates to next session open.
    _resolve_cron walks until elapsed-time deadline
    (_CRON_LOOKAHEAD_DAYS = 380; covers monthly crons with leap-year
    slack; yearly crons explicitly out of scope). All paths catch the
    lib's CalendarHorizonExceeded and convert to clear ValueError.
  - Modified `python/atp_strategy/api.py`: added CalendarHorizonExceeded
    and NotATradingSession (both subclass StrategyAPIError); extended
    TradingCalendar Protocol with premarket_open + afterhours_close +
    next_session; tightened StaticTradingCalendar to refuse fabricated
    boundary times on closed days (Protocol uniformity with
    UsEquityTradingCalendar).
  - Modified `python/atp_strategy/__init__.py`: re-exported
    UsEquityTradingCalendar, InMemoryScheduler, CalendarHorizonExceeded,
    NotATradingSession; added to __all__.
  - Modified `architecture/runtime_services.json`: added
    strategy_api_scheduler_contract block (required_scheduler_methods,
    required_calendar_methods, required_exchange_handles,

    calendar_horizon_end pinning constants, deferred[] documenting the
    CBOE alias + live-fire-loop ownership + pre/after-hours subscription
    routing ownership). Extended strategy_api.required_exports with

Override (CBOE alias):
- exchange_calendars ships no dedicated CBOE Options calendar
  (XCBO unavailable; XCBF is CBOE Futures with 16:15 ET close + Chicago
  tz — wrong asset class). NYSE / NASDAQ / CBOE-Options share the SIFMA
  U.S.-equity-class regular-session holiday calendar in practice for
  2026; the alias is correct for the strategy SDK's equity-class option
  workflows. CBOE-specific option-only early closes are deferred.
  Locked by CboeAliasDocumentedOverrideTest which asserts both the
  _EXCHANGE_HANDLES["CBOE"] = "XNYS" mapping AND the deferred[] string
  mentioning the alias rationale, so any silent regression trips the
  test. _EXCHANGE_HANDLES is the single point of update if a real
  handle lands. Owner: future feature shipping maintained CBOE Options
  session tables.

Date: 2026-05-15
Feature completed: SRS-ORCH-004 — Strategy Orchestrator records the
deployed code version (source hash + deployment timestamp) for each
strategy at deployment time and exposes it through a queryable
DeployedVersionRegistry port. SyRS SYS-79 wire form pinned at
`sha256:<64-hex>`; misformed hashes refused with
DEPLOYED_VERSION_INVALID before runtime.create; DeadlineExceeded
launches skip the version record (a version that was never deployed
must not appear in the active-strategy inventory or REST API
listing); deferred dashboard (SYS-41), REST API (IF-9), and backtest
result rows (SYS-21) will render the same canonical
version_identifier produced by DeployedVersion::version_identifier.

- Feat commit (72c6d47):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `OrderErrorCategory::DeployedVersionInvalid` variant with
    wire string `"DEPLOYED_VERSION_INVALID"`.
  * Added 3 spec-literal / validation-bound constants
    (SOURCE_HASH_ALGORITHM_PREFIX = "sha256:",
    SOURCE_HASH_DIGEST_HEX_LENGTH = 64, SOURCE_HASH_TOTAL_LENGTH = 71).
  * Added `SourceHash(String)` newtype with new() (infallible,
    matches ResourceProfile pattern — validation is at-boundary so
    test fixtures + env-var parsers can build the value the same
    way the gate does), validate() / validate_str() / as_str() /
    algorithm() / digest(). Validation enforces the `sha256:`
    prefix, the 64-hex-char length, AND rejects upper-case hex
    (the wire form is lower-case so round-trips are stable).
  * Added `SourceHashError` enum (4 variants): MissingAlgorithmPrefix,
    UnknownAlgorithm{found}, InvalidDigestLength{found, expected},
    NonHexDigest{found}.
  * Added `DeployedVersion { source_hash, deployed_at_seconds }`
    with new() / version_identifier(). The canonical form is
    `"<hash>@<timestamp>"` (the `@` separator avoids collision
    with the algorithm-prefix `:` and the hex alphabet) — single
    source of truth for the SYS-79 "same version identifier"
    guarantee. Forbidden-fields list (8 tokens) rejects
    docker_image / container_id / vendor / host_path / git_commit
    / git_branch / build_number / ci_run_id (coupling the audit
    shape to a build-system artifact would force multiple
    identifiers per code version, breaking the single-identifier
    guarantee).
  * Changed `StrategyLaunchRequest.deployment_hash: String →
    SourceHash` so the typed wrapper marks intent and the gate can
    validate at the orchestrator boundary.
  * Added `StrategyLaunchOutcome.deployed_version: DeployedVersion`

    request, violation)` factory mirroring the

- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added new port `DeployedVersionRegistry`:
      - `fn record(&self, strategy_id: &StrategyId, version:
        DeployedVersion) -> Result<(), DeployedVersionRegistryError>`
      - `fn lookup(&self, strategy_id: &StrategyId) ->
        Result<Option<DeployedVersion>, DeployedVersionRegistryError>`
    Both methods return Result so concrete adapters (durable-store
    outage, permission denied, registry desync) surface failures
    through the typed `DeployedVersionRegistryError`. Forbidden-
    imports list (sha2 / sha1 / md5 / blake3 / sled / rusqlite /
    redis / git2) keeps the orchestrator crate clean — concrete
    registry + hash-compute adapters live in separate crates that
    haven't shipped yet.
  * Added `DeployedVersionRegistryError { reason: String }` typed
    error struct with Display + std::error::Error.
  * Extended `launch()` with a 5th parameter `version_registry: &V`:
      1. Validate `request.deployment_hash.validate()` BEFORE
         `runtime.create` (defence in depth — rejection through
         `deployed_version_invalid(...)` with NO sink event, NO
         runtime mutation; no container exists to destroy).
      2. After resource-profile validation: `runtime.create` +
         `runtime.start`.
      3. On `ReadyWithinDeadline`: build `DeployedVersion::new(
         request.deployment_hash.clone(), observed_at_seconds)` and
         call `version_registry.record(...)`. Record failures are
         best-effort (matches WorkloadEventSink pattern) — the
         typed surface exists for concrete sinks and wrapping
         callers to observe.
      4. On `DeadlineExceeded`: skip the record (a version that
         was never deployed must not appear in the active-
         strategy inventory or REST API listing).
  * Added `deployed_version_for(request, observed_at_seconds)`
    helper that produces the same record the gate would build —
    callers can preview the version identifier without invoking
    the runtime port.
  * 5 new in-crate orchestrator tests covering: happy-path
    recording + outcome equality, DeadlineExceeded skipping
    record (ForbiddenVersionRegistry panics if touched),
    malformed-hash rejection without runtime invocation,
    record-failure-does-not-abort-launch (FlakyRegistry returning
    Err), helper-produces-same-record-as-launch.

enforces the SyRS SYS-57 workload-priority hierarchy against the
configured host memory safety margin (default 2048 MB; catalogue
floor/ceiling 256..1048576 MB). New workloads refused when the
post-admit host memory would dip below the margin; the lowest-priority
active *batch* workload is evicted when a higher-priority workload
arrives; live strategy execution is never selected for eviction
(SYS-58 last clause).
Status: 99 remaining features

  * Added 3 spec-literal / validation-bound constants
    (HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB_DEFAULT = 2048,
    _FLOOR = 256, _CEILING = 1_048_576).
  * Added `HostMemorySafetyMargin { mb: u32 }` with new() /
    default_margin() / validate() and `HostMemorySafetyMarginError`
    (BelowFloor / AboveCeiling).
  * Added `WorkloadPriority` enum (7 SYS-57 variants:
    LiveStrategy=1, MarketDataSubscriptionManager=2,
    PaperStrategy=3, NightlyDataIngestion=4, FactorPipeline=5,
    Backtest=6, Research=7) with rank() projection and
    `default_kind()` mapping. Forbidden-tokens list locks

    priority_class_id out so the enum stays categorical.

    and `WorkloadId(String)` newtype.

    { available_mb, safety_margin_mb }`.
  * Added `WorkloadAdmissionEvent` with 5 variants — Refused,
    Terminated, TerminationFailed (Docker / cgroup termination
    failure surfaced explicitly), HostProbeFailed (sysinfo / procfs
    probe failure), RegistryListingFailed (Docker engine timeout /
    in-process registry desync).
  * Added `StructuredOrchestratorError::host_memory_safety_margin_breach
    (request, available_mb, safety_margin_mb)` factory mirroring the
    `resource_profile_invalid` / `startup_deadline_exceeded`
    patterns. Updated the Rustdoc on the enclosing struct to name
    all three orchestrator-rejection categories.
  * 14 new in-crate unit tests covering the constants, validation
    paths, rank ordering, kind mapping, event variants, factory
    wire-string pin, and OrderErrorCategory mapping.
- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added three new ports:
      - `HostMemoryProbe { fn available_mb() -> Result<u64, HostMemoryProbeError> }`
      - `WorkloadRegistry { fn active() -> Result<Vec<RegisteredWorkload>, WorkloadRegistryError>; fn terminate(&WorkloadId) -> Result<(), WorkloadTerminationError> }`
      - `WorkloadEventSink { fn record(WorkloadAdmissionEvent) -> Result<(), WorkloadEventSinkError> }`
    Each carries a typed error surface. Forbidden-imports list
    (sysinfo / procfs / psutil / bollard / docker_api / shiplift /
    cgroups_rs) keeps the orchestrator crate clean — concrete
    adapters live in separate crates that haven't shipped yet.
  * Added 4 typed-error structs (HostMemoryProbeError,
    WorkloadRegistryError, WorkloadTerminationError {workload_id,
    reason}, WorkloadEventSinkError) with Display + std::error::Error.
  * Added `host_memory_safety_margin_default`,
    `safety_margin_from_lookup`, `safety_margin_via_env_lookup`,
    `safety_margin_from_env` (reads ATP_HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB
    distinguishing NotPresent / NotUnicode / unparseable / out-of-range).
  * Added `admit_workload(request, workload_id, priority,
    safety_margin, host, registry, sink, observed_at_seconds)`. The
    algorithm:
      1. Validate the safety margin (defence in depth — defends
         against programmatic override below the floor).
      2. Probe host memory; on Err emit HostProbeFailed event and
         refuse with HostMemorySafetyMarginBreach.
      3. Happy path: if available - needed >= margin, admit silently
         (no events, no registry mutation).
      4. Otherwise list active workloads; on Err emit
         RegistryListingFailed event and refuse.
      5. Pre-eviction feasibility: filter to Batch ∧ rank > new's
         rank, sort lowest-priority-first, sum recoverable mem.
         If even the full sum cannot reach the margin → refuse
         WITHOUT calling terminate (prevents partial-eviction-refusal
         where work is killed and admission still denied).
      6. Eviction loop: terminate each candidate; on Ok emit
         Terminated event + bank freed memory + early-return when
         post-admit headroom satisfies the margin; on Err emit
         TerminationFailed event with the typed reason and continue
         to the next candidate.
      7. Post-loop refusal: emit Refused event + return breach error.
    Live-immunity debug_assert pins the SyRS SYS-58 last-clause
    invariant inside the eviction loop. The launch() Rustdoc now
    states admit_workload is a REQUIRED PRECONDITION (the typed
    coupling via AdmissionToken / typestate is deferred to the
    production-caller session).
  * 18 new in-crate orchestrator tests covering admission happy
    path, refusal with no batch evictable, eviction success,
    lowest-priority-first ordering, Continuous immunity, Live
    immunity (debug_assert), feasibility-driven refusal without
    eviction, configurable margin override, env-var helper
    (default fallback, in-range override, unparseable, below-floor,
    NotUnicode), probe-error fail-closed, registry-active-error
    fail-closed, flaky-registry partial-failure (TerminationFailed
    event with typed reason), invalid-margin + probe-failure
    routing through HostProbeFailed.

        first calling admit_workload(). Override: the precondition is
        contract-level (launch()'s Rustdoc states the requirement
        explicitly); the typed-coupling fix via AdmissionToken
        typestate is named as a deferred entry in
        workload_priority_contract.deferred, scoped to land when the
        production caller of launch() lands (same owner, single
        parameter-list expansion).
      - adapter:sink-error-discard — admit_workload's `let _ = sink.record(...)`
        discards Results. Override: emission is best-effort by design
        (the admission decision is irreversible once made; sink
        errors do not abort or roll back); the typed
        WorkloadEventSinkError surface exists for concrete sinks and
        wrapping callers; gate-level capture with a richer return
        shape is named as a deferred entry, scoped to land alongside
        the concrete SRS-NOTIF-001 dispatcher when durable-delivery
        semantics make retry / propagation meaningful.
    1 warn (tests:missing-property): override accepted — the
    admission state space is small and finite (7 priorities × 2 kinds
    × bounded integers); the 12 in-crate + 7 integration + 6 domain
    tests cover it exhaustively plus error-path coverage; a property
    test would draw from the same finite space without exercising
    additional invariants.

- Feat commit (7d4f5a2):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `OrderErrorCategory::ResourceProfileInvalid` variant
    with wire string `"RESOURCE_PROFILE_INVALID"` — the SyRS
    SYS-64 single source of truth for the new rejection category.
  * Added 4 spec-literal constants (`LIVE_PROFILE_MEM_MB = 512`,
    `LIVE_PROFILE_CPU_HUNDREDTHS = 25`, `PAPER_PROFILE_MEM_MB = 300`,
    `PAPER_PROFILE_CPU_HUNDREDTHS = 10`) and 4 catalogue-aligned
    validation-bound constants (`RESOURCE_PROFILE_MEM_FLOOR_MB = 64`
    / `_MEM_CEILING_MB = 65536` / `_CPU_FLOOR_HUNDREDTHS = 5` /
    `_CPU_CEILING_HUNDREDTHS = 1600`).
  * Added `pub struct ResourceProfile { mem_mb: u32, cpu_hundredths:
    u32 }` with `live_default()`, `paper_default()`, `for_mode()`
    (mode-keyed dispatch with exhaustive match on StrategyMode), and
    `validate()` (enforces the SRS-ARCH-005 catalogue bounds).
    Forbidden-fields list: `cpu_cores_f32`, `cpu_cores`, `cpu_quota`,
    `memory_bytes`, `docker_image`, `container_id`, `vendor`,
    `host_path`, `cgroup_path`, `broker` (10 tokens) — locks float-CPU
    drift and vendor / container-runtime bleed out at the contract.
  * Added `pub enum ResourceProfileError` with 4 validation-failure
    variants (MemBelowFloor / MemAboveCeiling / CpuBelowFloor /
    CpuAboveCeiling).
  * Extended `StrategyLaunchRequest` and `StrategyLaunchOutcome` with
    `pub profile: ResourceProfile` (4 → 5 fields each). The
    forbidden-fields allowlist on each struct stays at 6 tokens
    (no docker_image / container_id / etc).
  * Added `StructuredOrchestratorError::resource_profile_invalid(
    request, violation)` factory mirroring the
    `startup_deadline_exceeded` pattern.
  * 12 new in-crate unit tests in atp-types covering the constant
    invariants, exhaustive destructure (proves only 2 fields), default
    invariance for live/paper, mode dispatch, all four validation
    failure paths, and the factory wire-string pin.
- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added a validation gate to `launch()` that calls
    `request.profile.validate()` BEFORE `runtime.create()` — on
    failure returns
    `StructuredOrchestratorError::resource_profile_invalid(...)` with
    NO sink event (no container exists to destroy; emitting an event
    would lie about a destroy that never happened — Pattern A,
    matches ERR-4/5/6 structured-rejection).
  * Threaded `request.profile` through the happy-path outcome:
    `StrategyLaunchOutcome { ..., profile: request.profile }`. The
    contract block enforces `profile: request.profile` literally
    appears at the construction site (no silent re-defaulting).
  * Added `live_profile_default()`, `paper_profile_default()`,
    `profile_for_mode(mode)` re-exporters on `StrategyOrchestrator`
    so callers don't have to reach into atp-types.
  * Built the env-var → launch-profile WIRE (the substantive
    enhancement the user requested): three new functions on
    `StrategyOrchestrator`:
      - `profile_for_mode_from_lookup<F: Fn(&str) -> Option<String>>`
        — pure, lookup-based; tests drive it with stub maps.
      - `profile_for_mode_via_env_lookup<F: Fn(&str) ->
        Result<String, std::env::VarError>>` — testable bridge
        that distinguishes `VarError::NotPresent` (silently falls
        back to SyRS default) from `VarError::NotUnicode` (returns
        a structured `ResourceProfileEnvError::Unparseable*` —
        a set-but-invalid override is the OPPOSITE of "configuration
        overrides are validated" so it must surface, not collapse).
      - `profile_for_mode_from_env(mode)` — production wrapper that
        plugs `std::env::var` into `_via_env_lookup`.
    Reads ATP_LIVE_STRATEGY_MEM_MB / _CPU and ATP_PAPER_STRATEGY_MEM_MB
    / _CPU; converts cores → hundredths AT THE BOUNDARY (CPU stored
    as f64 in catalogue, u32 hundredths in atp-types); validates the
    f64 cores against the f64 catalogue bounds (0.05..16.0) BEFORE
    rounding to u32 hundredths, so 0.046 cores is rejected as
    below-floor instead of silently rounding up to 5 hundredths and
    passing the integer check (symmetric for above-ceiling 16.004).
    The 1e-9 tolerance in the f64 bounds-check absorbs binary-float
    representation noise without rejecting the exact floor / ceiling.
  * Added `pub enum ResourceProfileEnvError` (UnparseableMem /
    UnparseableCpu / Validation(ResourceProfileError) variants)
    with Display + std::error::Error. The `From<ResourceProfileError>`
    impl lets the `?` operator collapse validation errors into the
    env-error envelope cleanly.
  * 14 new in-crate unit tests covering: the validation gate
    (happy-path, 4 rejection variants), the env-var wire (defaults,
    in-range overrides, unparseable mem / cpu, below-floor /
    above-ceiling, exact-floor / exact-ceiling boundary, NotPresent
    fallback, NotUnicode rejection on mem AND cpu, present-value
    threading).
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json`:
  * Added `resource_profile_contract` block (~155 lines) with
    spec_constants / validation_constants / resource_profile shape +

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **Concrete Docker StrategyContainerRuntime is still deferred.**
  Same shape as SESSION 20's audit conclusion: the Rust workspace
  is fully sync (zero tokio / async); a bollard-based driver implies
  a workspace-wide async refactor or a `block_on()` anti-pattern.
  No forcing function until either (a) SRS-ORCH-003 workload-priority
  arbitration lands and needs to actually destroy containers when
  the host margin is breached, or (b) a Rust orchestrator service
  binary is built that calls launch() against a real runtime
  (today main.py is still `pass` and there is no Rust binary).
- **Typed error surface on the lifecycle port is paired with the
  Docker driver.** create / stop / restart / destroy currently
  return unit. When the Docker driver lands, those signatures need
  a typed error variant (e.g.
  `Result<(), ContainerRuntimeError>` covering cgroup-creation
  failure, insufficient host resources, network failures). This is
  SRS-ORCH-001 trait-signature retrofit scope; the
  resource_profile_contract.deferred list names it.
- **Real next P1 by orchestrator-family ID order:**
  **SRS-ORCH-003** (enforce workload priority when the host memory
  safety margin would be breached). Has all the prerequisite
  infrastructure ready:
  - `ATP_HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB` env var with default 2048,
    min 256, max 1048576 in the catalogue (SRS-ARCH-005 PASS).
  - `ResourceProfile` types and `validate()` method available from
    this session.
  - The 5 priority slots SyRS SYS-57 names — live strategy >
    market data subscription > paper strategies > nightly ingestion >
    factor pipeline > backtest > research — would need a new
    `WorkloadPriority` enum in atp-types with the same exhaustive-
    destructure invariant SRS-ORCH-001 / SRS-ORCH-002 used, plus a
    new gate function on `StrategyOrchestrator` that consults host
    memory before allowing a launch.
  - Same 3-commit cadence: prep (extend SAFETY_PATH_RE with
    `workload[_-]?priority` and `host[_-]?memory[_-]?margin`), feat
    (types + gate + contract block + check script + integration
    test + L7 domain test), chore (flip passes:true + record
    SESSION 22 progress notes).
- **SRS-ORCH-004** (deployment version surface) is the third
  orchestrator-family P1 — deployment_hash is already on
  StrategyLaunchRequest from SRS-ORCH-001, but the dashboard /
  REST surface for it is deferred.
- **Codex CLI requires a recent version.** During this session
  `codex exec` initially failed with `'gpt-5.5' model requires a
  newer version of Codex` — operator upgraded codex mid-session and
  it worked. The /codex:adversarial-review SLASH COMMAND has
  `disable-model-invocation` set so Claude cannot invoke it via the
  Skill tool (memory: [[feedback-codex-adversarial-review]]); the
  `codex exec` CLI bypass is the working automation path.

=== SESSION 19 ===
Date: 2026-05-14
Feature completed: SRS-ORCH-001 — Strategy Orchestrator owns strategy
container lifecycle (SyRS SYS-10): launch / observe-health gates flow
exclusively through StrategyContainerRuntime + HealthCheckEventSink
ports, the NFR-P9 30-second startup budget is enforced via
LaunchReadiness, an over-deadline launch destroys the half-launched
container BEFORE recording the dashboard event (SRS-ORCH-002 / SyRS
SYS-57 resource release; ordered destroy-then-record so a sink
failure cannot mask the resource release), and an Unresponsive
container is atomically restarted AND surfaced on the dashboard
(SYS-13 selectivity: a Healthy probe is read-only). AC-12 boundary
(no strategy may manage another container) stays enforced by the
existing dependency_boundary_check `atp_orchestrator` forbidden
import already on every lower-layer crate.

What I did:
- Prep commit (7064c49): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  `tools/critic_check.py` to add `orchestrator[_-]?lifecycle` and
  `strategy[_-]?container` tokens. Continues the per-feature
  precedent (ERR-4 added subscription_limit + market_data_line, ERR-5
  added ingestion_validation + record_quarantine, ERR-6 added
  pacing_budget + ingestion_schedule). The L7 domain test at
  `tests/domain/test_orchestrator_lifecycle.py` and the contract
  tool at `tools/orchestrator_lifecycle_check.py` now trigger
  safety:paired-test-required if a future change touches either
  side.
- Feat commit (00389d5):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `StrategyStartupDeadlineExceeded` variant to
    `OrderErrorCategory` (now 10 variants) with wire string
    `"STRATEGY_STARTUP_DEADLINE_EXCEEDED"` — single source of truth
    for the SyRS SYS-64 wire vocabulary; no parallel enum.
  * Added `pub const STRATEGY_STARTUP_DEADLINE_MS: u64 = 30_000` —
    the NFR-P9 30-second budget single source of truth. Future
    tuning has exactly one site.
  * Added `pub enum ContainerLifecycleAction { Create, Start, Stop,
    Restart, Destroy }` with `as_str()` map. Five variants exactly
    cover the SyRS SYS-10 lifecycle vocabulary; an exhaustive match
    would fail to compile if a variant were dropped.
  * Added `pub enum ContainerHealthState { Healthy, Unresponsive }`
    with `is_unresponsive()` helper. Two-state SYS-13 auto-restart
    trigger classifier.
  * Added `pub enum LaunchReadiness { ReadyWithinDeadline {
    elapsed_millis }, DeadlineExceeded { elapsed_millis,
    deadline_millis } }`. Struct-variant enum: the elapsed time is
    available on BOTH branches so the dashboard can render
    percentile histograms without re-probing; the deadline is
    carried on the exceeded variant for TOCTOU closure (same
    rationale as ERR-4 / ERR-6's "carry the limit on the event").
  * Added `pub struct StrategyLaunchRequest { strategy_id,
    mode: StrategyMode, deployment_hash: String, deadline_millis:
    u64 }`. Four fields, deliberately no docker_image /
    container_id / host_path / vendor / broker / ib_session_id
    (forbidden-list locked by the contract block).
  * Added `pub struct StrategyLaunchOutcome { strategy_id,
    ready_within_deadline: bool, elapsed_millis: u64,
    deadline_millis: u64 }`. Four fields, same forbidden-list.
  * Added `pub struct ContainerHealthEvent { state:
    ContainerHealthState, strategy_id, action_taken:
    ContainerLifecycleAction, observed_at_seconds: u64 }`.
    Carrying `action_taken` on the event closes a TOCTOU window —
    the dashboard can render "restarted at T" / "destroyed at T"
    without a second probe.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredOrchestratorError` with factory
    `startup_deadline_exceeded(request, elapsed_millis,
    deadline_millis)`. Reuses
    `OrderErrorCategory::StrategyStartupDeadlineExceeded` as the
    wire-string source of truth (mirrors the
    StructuredPacingError / StructuredIngestionError /
    StructuredSubscriptionError pattern).
  * Added 8 in-crate unit tests in `atp-types` covering: action
    enum exhaustiveness, health-state exhaustiveness, readiness
    enum payload shape, the NFR-P9 constant value, the
    exhaustive-destructure proof of "exactly four fields" for each
    new struct, and the factory's wire-string / message /
    Display-format invariants.
- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `trait StrategyContainerRuntime` with six methods:
    create, start (returns LaunchReadiness), stop, restart, destroy,
    health (returns ContainerHealthState). The trait lives in
    `atp-orchestrator` (NOT `atp-types`) because the consumer
    lives here; lower-layer crates cannot import
    `atp_orchestrator` (dependency_boundary_check already lists it
    as a forbidden token).
  * Added `trait HealthCheckEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    ContainerHealthEvent); }` — the structured-event publication
    channel (dashboard WebSocket + SRS-LOG-001 audit log +
    SRS-NOTIF-001 dispatcher fan-out, all deferred to those
    features).
  * Added `pub fn launch<R, S>(&self, request:
    StrategyLaunchRequest, runtime: &R, sink: &S,
    observed_at_seconds: u64) -> Result<StrategyLaunchOutcome,
    StructuredOrchestratorError>`. Matches on
    `LaunchReadiness`; ReadyWithinDeadline returns
    `StrategyLaunchOutcome` (the ONLY construction site);
    DeadlineExceeded calls `runtime.destroy(&request.strategy_id)`
    FIRST (SRS-ORCH-002 / SyRS SYS-57 resource release), THEN
    `sink.record(ContainerHealthEvent { action_taken: Destroy,
    ... })`, THEN returns the structured error. The ordering is
    statically required by the contract — a sink failure must not
    mask the resource release.
  * Added `pub fn observe_health<R, S>(&self, strategy_id, runtime,
    sink, observed_at_seconds) -> ContainerHealthState`. Matches
    on `ContainerHealthState`; Healthy returns the state read-only
    (no runtime mutation, no event); Unresponsive calls
    `runtime.restart(&strategy_id)` AND `sink.record(...)` in one
    transaction (SYS-13's atomic auto-restart + dashboard
    fan-out).
  * Added `pub const fn startup_deadline_millis(&self) -> u64`
    that re-exports the `atp-types` constant so callers can
    populate `deadline_millis` without reaching into `atp-types`.
  * Added 6 in-crate unit tests covering the gate happy-path,
    refusal, destroy-call assertion, no-op-on-healthy,
    auto-restart-on-unresponsive, and exactly-once-probe.
- Added `crates/atp-orchestrator/tests/orch_1_lifecycle_contract.rs`:
  * Spy implementations of both ports with per-method call
    counters and a Forbidden* sink that panics if invoked
    (matches the ERR-3 / ERR-5 / ERR-6 pattern).
  * Six integration tests anchoring the post-conditions
    behaviourally: ReadyWithinDeadline outcome + zero event,
    DeadlineExceeded refusal + destroy_calls == 1 +
    stop_calls == 0 + restart_calls == 0 + exactly one event,
    Healthy probe read-only, Unresponsive probe restart +
    event-once + zero destroy/stop, mode-uniformity (Live and
    Paper launches share envelope shape), zero-acceptance on
    refusal.
- Added `architecture/runtime_services.json` orchestrator_lifecycle_contract
  block (180 lines): types-crate + orchestrator-crate, all five
  declared enums/structs with required + forbidden fields, the
  NFR-P9 constant declaration, the two port declarations, both
  entry points with full guard metadata including:
  * launch_guard.runtime_destroy_call = "runtime.destroy"
  * launch_guard.exceeded_action_taken =
    "ContainerLifecycleAction::Destroy"
  * launch_guard.forbidden_mutations: 10 tokens (containers.insert
    / registry.add / self.spawn_container / self.suppress_event
    etc. — every plausible regression path)
  * health_observe_guard.forbidden_mutations_on_healthy: 6 tokens
    (runtime.restart / runtime.destroy / sink.record /
    self.notify_dashboard etc. — the SYS-13 selectivity invariant)
  * 6 deferred-list entries naming the concrete Docker driver,
    SRS-ORCH-002 resource-profile enforcement, SRS-ORCH-003
    workload-priority arbitration, SRS-ORCH-004 deployment-version
    surface, the concrete sink wiring, and restart back-off.
- Added `tools/orchestrator_lifecycle_check.py` (683 lines):
  * 11 static checks (lifecycle action enum, health state enum,
    launch readiness enum, three struct shape checks with
    forbidden-field allowlist, NFR-P9 constant value check, two
    port trait checks, the two entry-point guards).
  * Inline `_variant_arm` helper (not in
    `tools/_rust_parser.py` — that hoist is still tracked) so the
    check can handle struct-variant match arms (the existing
    `_match_arm` from error_handling_check only handles unit
    variants).
  * The launch guard check enforces: presence of runtime.start,
    presence of runtime.destroy, presence of sink.record,
    presence of the action_taken token, presence of the rejection
    category or factory call, ABSENCE of any forbidden_mutations
    token, AND the positional invariant `destroy_pos < sink_pos`
    (so a refactor that swaps order would be caught).
  * The observe-health guard check enforces: presence of
    runtime.health, presence of runtime.restart inside the
    Unresponsive arm, presence of sink.record inside the
    Unresponsive arm, AND ABSENCE of any forbidden mutation
    inside the Healthy arm.
  * `assert_orchestrator_lifecycle_static(config, root)` returns
    the 11-bullet evidence list for `tools/architecture_check.py`
    to consume without invoking cargo.
  * cargo smoke (`cargo test -p atp-orchestrator --lib` + the new
    integration test file) gates the final PASS bullet.
- Wired into `tools/architecture_check.py`: import the static

  clause. The current HealthCheckEventSink is a port only.

=== SESSION 18 ===
Date: 2026-05-13
Feature completed: ERR-6 — IB pacing budget exceeded by configured
ingestion job: refuse over-budget jobs at scheduling time at the
DataLayer layer, publish a structured PacingBudgetEvent carrying both
projected_requests AND permitted_requests for dashboard fan-out
(TOCTOU closure), and produce zero start-side-effect on the scheduler
(traces SRS-DATA-002 + SRS-DATA-004 + SyRS SYS-31 / SYS-55 / SYS-22b /
SYS-23 + StRS A-10 / SN-1.26 / SN-1.27).
Status: 102 remaining features

What I did:
- Prep commit (24391a0): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  `tools/critic_check.py` to add `pacing[_-]?budget` and
  `ingestion[_-]?schedule` to the safety-path alternation. Continues
  the per-feature precedent (ERR-2 added connectivity, ERR-3 added
  stale_data, ERR-4 added subscription_limit + market_data_line in
  SESSION 16 commit 8143ac5, ERR-5 added ingestion_validation +
  record_quarantine in SESSION 17 commit ff10ef0). The split-commit
  shape exactly mirrors SESSIONs 16 + 17.
- Feat commit (2bfa1c4):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `IngestionPacingBudgetExceeded` variant to
    `OrderErrorCategory` (now 9 variants) with wire string
    `"INGESTION_PACING_BUDGET_EXCEEDED"` — single source of truth for
    the SyRS SYS-64 wire vocabulary; no parallel enum.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionJobRequest { job_kind: String,
    window_seconds: u64 }` — vendor-neutral schedule envelope.
    Deliberately omits broker / IB session / tick / vendor-dataset /
    vendor-table / parquet-path / credential fields (caught by the
    contract block's 7-element forbidden_fields allowlist).
  * Added `pub enum PacingBudgetState { WithinBudget, BudgetExceeded }`
    with `const is_exceeded()` helper. 2-state cadence mirrors ERR-4's
    SubscriptionLimitState.
  * Added `pub struct PacingBudgetEvent { state, job_kind,
    projected_requests: u32, permitted_requests: u32,
    observed_at_seconds: u64 }` — exactly five fields, no
    broker/session/vendor/tick leakage. Carrying BOTH projected AND
    permitted closes a TOCTOU window (same rationale as ERR-4's
    current_lines + configured_limit). `job_kind` semantically encodes
    the window (minute-bar-watchlist → SYS-22b overnight,
    option-chain-capture → SYS-23 near-close), so no separate
    window_label field.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredPacingError { category, error_type,
    message, original_request: IngestionJobRequest }` with a
    category-pinned factory `budget_exceeded(request, projected,
    permitted)` that `debug_assert!`s the category stays
    `OrderErrorCategory::IngestionPacingBudgetExceeded`. Implements
    `fmt::Display` and `std::error::Error`. Message format:
    `"SRS-DATA-002 + SRS-DATA-004 + SyRS SYS-55: ingestion job <kind>
    over pacing budget — projected <N> requests, permitted <M>"`.
  * Added 5 new unit tests: PacingBudgetState predicate,
    IngestionJobRequest + PacingBudgetEvent exhaustive destructures
    (forbidden-field proofs), TOCTOU pairing assertion (projected
    >= permitted on BudgetExceeded), factory wire-string + Display
    round-trip. Total atp-types unit tests: 25 (was 20 in SESSION 17).
  * Extended the existing
    `order_error_category_wire_strings_track_syrs_sys_64` test to
    cover the 9th variant.
- Extended `crates/atp-data/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait PacingBudgetValidator` with three read-only
    methods: `projected_requests`, `permitted_requests`,
    `check_budget`. The trait has NO mutator method — the
    zero-job-start invariant is anchored at the port shape so a
    concrete validator cannot dispatch the job through the probe
    call.
  * Added `pub trait PacingBudgetEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    PacingBudgetEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (deferred) route events
    to logs, the dashboard scheduling-view alert pane, and the
    notification dispatcher per SyRS SYS-55's "until scope or window
    configuration is reduced" clause.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionJobScheduled { job_kind: String }` —
    only construction site is the `WithinBudget` arm of
    `schedule_ingestion_job`.
  * Added `DataLayer::schedule_ingestion_job<V, S>(schedule,
    validator, events, observed_at_seconds) -> Result<
    IngestionJobScheduled, StructuredPacingError>` with the match:
    `WithinBudget => Ok(IngestionJobScheduled { ... })`,
    `BudgetExceeded => { let projected =
    validator.projected_requests(&schedule); let permitted =
    validator.permitted_requests(&schedule); events.record(
    PacingBudgetEvent { ... });
    Err(StructuredPacingError::budget_exceeded(schedule, projected,
    permitted)) }`. Takes NO `StrategyMode` parameter — SyRS SYS-55
    applies the same pacing-budget rule independent of which strategy
    is live; the scheduled ingestion jobs precede mode selection.
  * Added `#[doc(hidden)] pub const _PACING_BUDGET_CATEGORY:
    OrderErrorCategory = OrderErrorCategory::IngestionPacingBudgetExceeded;`
    workspace-level reference to the canonical wire-string source.
    Mirrors ERR-4's `_SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY` and ERR-5's
    `_INGESTION_VALIDATION_CATEGORY`.
  * Added 3 new in-crate unit tests: WithinBudget happy path with
    `PacingBudgetForbiddenSink`, BudgetExceeded rejection with one
    event, validator call-count sanity (CountingValidator wrapper
    asserts check_budget probed once + projected/permitted each read
    once on the rejection leaf). Total atp-data unit tests: 7 (was 4
    in SESSION 17).
- Added `crates/atp-data/tests/err_6_pacing_budget_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 5 tests, ~456 lines):
  * `PacingBudgetValidatorSpy` (parameterized state + projected +
    permitted + per-method call counters), `PacingBudgetEventSinkSpy`
    (collects events), `PacingBudgetForbiddenSink` (panics on

    permitted), exactly one event recorded with all five fields,

    for minute-bar-watchlist and option-chain-capture (category +

- Feat commit (40fef50):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `IngestionRecordValidationFailed` variant to
    `OrderErrorCategory` (now 8 variants) with wire string
    `"INGESTION_RECORD_VALIDATION_FAILED"` — single source of truth
    for the SyRS SYS-64 wire vocabulary; no parallel enum.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionRecordSubmission { source: String,
    record_hash: String }` — vendor-neutral envelope. Deliberately
    omits broker / IB session / tick / vendor-dataset / vendor-table /
    parquet-path / credential fields (caught by the contract block's
    7-element forbidden_fields allowlist).
  * Added `pub enum QuarantineReason` — Copy/Hash/PartialEq/Eq 6-
    variant enum mapping 1:1 to the SyRS SYS-77 rules (a..f):
    RangeViolation, OhlcOutOfBand, NegativeVolume, NullRequiredField,
    DuplicateRecord, OptionFieldMissing. SCREAMING_SNAKE wire strings
    via `as_str()`. Copy + Hash so dashboards can aggregate by reason
    via a HashMap key without scanning a string.
  * Added `pub enum RecordValidationOutcome { Valid,
    Quarantined(QuarantineReason) }` with `is_quarantined()` helper.
    2-state cadence mirrors ERR-4's WithinLimit/ExceededLimit; reason
    is carried in-band as a payload (clean separation of state vs.
    reason — different from a flat 7-variant enum).
  * Added `pub struct IngestionValidationEvent { state, reason,
    source, record_hash, observed_at_seconds }` — exactly five
    fields, no broker/session/vendor/tick leakage. `state` and
    `reason` are redundant by design (mirrors ERR-4's state +
    numerics) so sinks don't need to destructure the outcome.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredIngestionError { category,
    error_type, message, original_record: IngestionRecordSubmission }`
    with a category-pinned factory `quarantined(record, reason)` that
    `debug_assert!`s the category stays
    `OrderErrorCategory::IngestionRecordValidationFailed`. Implements
    `fmt::Display` and `std::error::Error`. Message format:
    `"SRS-DATA-013 + SyRS SYS-77: record <hash> from <source>
    quarantined — <REASON_WIRE_STRING>"`.

    QuarantineReason wire strings, RecordValidationOutcome

- Extended `crates/atp-data/src/lib.rs` (was a 26-line stub; now ~245
  lines including unit tests):
  * Added `pub trait RecordValidator { fn validate(&self, record:
    &IngestionRecordSubmission) -> RecordValidationOutcome; }`. The
    trait has NO mutator method — the zero-write-to-primary
    invariant is anchored at the port shape so a concrete validator
    cannot commit a record through the probe call.
  * Added `pub trait IngestionValidationEventSink { fn record(&self,
    event: IngestionValidationEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (deferred)

  * Added `DataLayer::ingest_record<V, S>(record,
    validator, events, observed_at_seconds) -> Result<IngestionAccepted,
    StructuredIngestionError>` with the match:
    `Valid => Ok(IngestionAccepted { ... })`,
    `Quarantined(reason) => { events.record(IngestionValidationEvent
    { ... }); Err(StructuredIngestionError::quarantined(record,
    reason)) }`. Takes NO `StrategyMode` parameter — SyRS SYS-77
    applies the same six rules uniformly across every ingestion
    source.

    OrderErrorCategory = OrderErrorCategory::IngestionRecordValidationFailed;`

=== SESSION 16 ===
Date: 2026-05-12
Feature completed: ERR-4 — Market-data line limit exceeded: reject the
subscription request with SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED at the
MarketDataSubscriptionManager layer, publish a structured
SubscriptionLimitEvent carrying both current_lines AND configured_limit
for dashboard fan-out, and produce zero mutation on the subscription
registry (traces SRS-MD-002 + SyRS SYS-70 + SyRS SYS-64 identical-
contract + StRS A-13 ~100-line ballpark)
Status: 104 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub struct SubscriptionRequest { strategy_id, symbol }` —
    the source-neutral request envelope the manager gates on
    (mirrors OrderSubmission minus quantity, since a subscription has
    no order semantics).
  * Added `pub enum SubscriptionLimitState { WithinLimit, ExceededLimit }`
    with a `const is_exceeded()` helper. ExceededLimit types the
    SRS-MD-002 / SYS-70 rejection path.
  * Added `pub struct SubscriptionLimitEvent { state, strategy_id,
    symbol, current_lines: u32, configured_limit: u32 }` — exactly five
    fields, no broker/session/vendor/tick leakage. Carrying BOTH
    current_lines AND configured_limit closes a TOCTOU window: the
    configured value can be re-tuned between rejection and dashboard
    render, so the event is self-describing.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredSubscriptionError { category:
    OrderErrorCategory, error_type, message, original_request:
    SubscriptionRequest }` with a category-pinned factory
    `limit_reached(request, current, limit)` that constructs the
    rejection envelope and `debug_assert!`s the category stays
    `OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached`. Reuses the
    pre-declared OrderErrorCategory variant as the single source of
    truth for the SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED wire string (no parallel
    enum — that would be a SYS-64 invariant violation waiting to
    happen the next time someone adds a category).
  * Added 4 new unit tests: WithinLimit / ExceededLimit predicate
    coverage, `SubscriptionLimitEvent` exhaustive destructure (proves
    no extra public fields), StRS A-13 current_lines + configured_limit
    sanity (~100-line ballpark), and the factory wire-string + Display
    round-trip. Total atp-types unit tests: 15 (was 11 in SESSION 15).
- Extended `crates/atp-market-data/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait SubscriptionLineCounter { fn lines_in_use(&self)
    -> u32; fn line_limit(&self) -> u32; fn try_acquire(&self, request:
    &SubscriptionRequest) -> SubscriptionLimitState; }`. The port owns
    the line accounting (concrete impl backed by
    `ATP_MARKET_DATA_LINE_LIMIT` and the live subscription set is
    deferred to SRS-MD-001 / SRS-MD-007). `try_acquire` is read-only
    with respect to the registry — admission happens after the manager
    observes `WithinLimit`.
  * Added `pub trait SubscriptionLimitEventSink { fn record(&self,
    event: SubscriptionLimitEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (later) route
    events to logs (SRS-LOG-001), the dashboard WebSocket alert pane
    (SyRS SYS-70's "alert the operator on the dashboard" clause), and
    the notification dispatcher.
  * Added `pub struct SubscriptionAccepted { strategy_id, symbol }` as
    the happy-path envelope. The static check pins it as the only
    construction site inside the WithinLimit arm.
  * Added `MarketDataSubscriptionManager::request_subscription<C, S>(...)
    -> Result<SubscriptionAccepted, StructuredSubscriptionError>` with
    the match: `WithinLimit => Ok(SubscriptionAccepted { ... })`,
    `ExceededLimit => { current = counter.lines_in_use();
    limit = counter.line_limit(); events.record(SubscriptionLimitEvent {
    ... });
    Err(StructuredSubscriptionError::limit_reached(request, current,
    limit)) }`. The gate takes NO `StrategyMode` parameter — SyRS SYS-64
    mandates an identical error contract for live and paper modes, and
    SyRS SYS-70 places the gate over the consolidated subscription set
    for all active strategies regardless of mode.
  * Added `#[doc(hidden)] pub const _SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY:
    OrderErrorCategory = OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached;`
    as a workspace-level reference to the canonical wire-string source
    so a future dead-code scan cannot drop the link.
  * Added 3 new in-crate unit tests: WithinLimit happy path with
    forbidden-sink-equivalent, ExceededLimit rejection with one event,
    and a counter-call-count sanity test proving `try_acquire` is
    consulted exactly once per request. Total atp-market-data unit
    tests: 4 (was 1 in SESSION 15).
- Added `crates/atp-market-data/tests/err_4_subscription_limit_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 5 tests):
  * `LineCounterSpy` (parameterized state + current_lines +
    configured_limit + per-method call counters), `EventSinkSpy`
    (collects every recorded event), `ForbiddenSink` (panics on
    `record()`) for cross-state isolation.
  * `err_4_exceeded_state_blocks_request_with_structured_error` — full
    ERR-4 contract: error category is `SubscriptionLimitReached`, wire
    string `"SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED"`, exactly one event recorded
    with `state == ExceededLimit`, `current_lines == 100`,
    `configured_limit == 100`, correct strategy_id and symbol; counter
    probed exactly once for try_acquire / lines_in_use / line_limit.
    Message asserts trace strings (SRS-MD-002, SYS-70, strategy,
    symbol, limit value).
  * `err_4_within_limit_state_returns_accepted_and_emits_no_event` —
    negative control with the `ForbiddenSink` panic stub: WithinLimit
    must accept and must NOT record an event; counter probed for
    try_acquire only (the WithinLimit leaf doesn't populate an event,
    so lines_in_use / line_limit must not be read).
  * `err_4_exceeded_state_holds_across_many_requests` — pseudo-property
    sweep across 5 (strategy, symbol, current_lines, configured_limit)
    cases including ranges [100..9999], paper and live strategy_ids:
    zero acceptances, exactly 5 events with per-case current_lines and
    configured_limit correctly recorded; try_acquire probed exactly
    `cases.len()` times.
  * `err_4_identical_contract_for_live_and_paper_subscribers` — SYS-64
    invariant: the rejection envelope is byte-identical for a
    strategy_id naming a live strategy and one naming a paper strategy
    (category + error_type + wire string equal across modes;
    original_request and message differ by design — they carry the
    per-caller payload). Two events recorded with identical state and
    numerics, only strategy_id differing.
  * `err_4_exceeded_state_anchors_zero_mutation_via_port_shape` — the
    zero-registry-mutation invariant anchored at the port-shape level:
    the SubscriptionLineCounter trait exposes NO mutator method, so
    the manager cannot move the in-use count through the public port
    API. The PRIMARY enforcement is the static check's
    `forbidden_mutations` allowlist (13 patterns: registry.insert / add
    / push, subscriptions.insert / push / add, request.acquire,
    counter.acquire / commit / reserve, lines.increment, self.register,
    self.add_subscription); this Rust test anchors the behavioral
    post-condition. (Renamed from
    `err_4_exceeded_state_does_not_mutate_subscription_registry` after
    the judgment-pass critic flagged the original assertion as
    tautological — see Critic verdicts below.)

Critic verdicts:
  COMMIT 1 (feat(ERR-4) — bdb4c29):
    deterministic: APPROVE — 0 findings
    judgment (general-purpose sub-agent, fresh context): APPROVE — 0
      findings. Reviewer cross-checked architecture (port placement
      at atp-market-data preserves SRS-ARCH-002 dependency direction
      — atp-execution and atp-market-data are sibling crates with no
      cross-edge), wire-string source-of-truth (single — verified
      that "SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED" appears as a literal only at
      atp-types::OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached.as_str
      and inside its existing unit test; no parallel enum), SYS-64
      identical-contract test scope (correct — compares category +
      error_type + wire string; excludes message and original_request
      as they carry per-caller payload by design), SRS-MD-002 letter-
      compliance (subscription-manager gate satisfies the acceptance
      criterion; ERR-4b order-path bubble-up correctly deferred as
      separate scope), dashboard-alert posture (matches ERR-2 / ERR-3
      — structured event through a port, concrete dashboard subscriber
      deferred to UI-* features), atomic-commit hygiene (every file
      strictly required by ERR-4; no incidental refactors). The
      first judgment pass had returned `block` on
      `meta:critic-self-modification` because the original diff
      included a `tools/critic_check.py` SAFETY_PATH_RE extension;
      that change was deliberately moved to commit 2 (chore(critic))
      per the autonomous-agent workflow's "only humans bypass" rule.
      The first pass had also flagged two substantive `warn`s; both
      were addressed before commit 1 landed (zero-mutation L7 test
      renamed to anchor port-shape semantics rather than the
      previously-tautological before-after counter snapshot; the
      contract's `forbidden_mutations` allowlist extended from 6 to
