  COMMIT 2 (chore(critic) — 8143ac5):
    deterministic: APPROVE — 0 findings
    judgment: would BLOCK by rule `meta:critic-self-modification`
      (the literal refusal clause #4 in `prompts/critic_prompt.md`).
      Per the autonomous-agent workflow, only humans bypass this
      meta-block; the operator explicitly signed off via the
      AskUserQuestion "Split into two commits" path. The block is
      unconditional by design — it is the gate's reviewer-facing
      trigger for changes to itself. The override is recorded in the
      commit message and here so shell history and commit metadata
      both carry the audit trail.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **ERR-4b (deferred):** SRS-MD-002 also requires the line-limit
  gate to fire when an order is placed against a symbol with no
  existing subscription — `submit_live_order` would acquire a line
  via the subscription manager and surface `SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED`
  through the existing `StructuredOrderError` envelope (which is
  why the variant is pre-declared in `OrderErrorCategory`). This
  adds another port to `submit_live_order`'s signature (now at five
  ports; would become six). Next session should:
  (a) introduce `LiveSubscriptionAcquirer` (or similar) at the
      execution layer with a method that delegates to the subscription
      manager;
  (b) thread it through `submit_live_order` as a sixth port
      reference, nested inside the existing Connected + Fresh leaf
      (the deepest happy path);
  (c) extend `tools/error_handling_check.py` (or its peer) with a
      static check that the order-submission path also produces
      `SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED` when the line-limit gate fails;
  (d) add an `err_4b_*` integration test in
      `crates/atp-execution/tests/`;
  (e) add a new feature_list.json entry for ERR-4b (it does not
      currently exist).
- **Concrete `SubscriptionLineCounter` impl** wired to
  `ATP_MARKET_DATA_LINE_LIMIT` and the live subscription set. The
  actual bookkeeping (the set of open lines, dedup of multi-strategy
  subscriptions to the same symbol per SyRS SYS-70) belongs to
  SRS-MD-001 / SRS-MD-007. ERR-4 ships only the port shape and the
  gate; SRS-MD-001 plugs in the concrete state holder.
- The `request_subscription` signature now takes two port references
  (counter + events). Any future feature that adds a new
  subscription-manager guard (e.g., rotation / priority queuing per
  StRS A-13 if the line limit is over-subscribed) should follow the
  same pattern: introduce a port trait at the market-data layer,
  extend the signature, and nest the new match inside the appropriate
  existing arm.
- The `OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached` variant is now
  consumed by `atp-market-data` via the
  `StructuredSubscriptionError::limit_reached` factory and a hidden
  `_SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY` const. The constant guards against a
  future dead-code scan dropping the link between the wire string and
  this crate. If a third caller emerges (likely ERR-4b at
  atp-execution), consider promoting the constant out of `doc(hidden)`
  or hoisting a shared helper.
- The `error_type` field for the rejection is
  `"SubscriptionLimitReached"` (CamelCase, like ERR-2's
  `"IbGatewayUnreachable"` and ERR-3's `"MarketDataStale"`). The
  SESSION 14 note about avoiding snake_case tokens inside core crates
  still applies: `market_data` could collide with the SRS-ARCH-002
  dependency-boundary regex if a future error_type uses it.
- `tools/subscription_limit_check.py` reuses `_trait_body` from
  `tools/connectivity_check.py`, `_struct_body` / `_enum_body` from
  `tools/historical_data_check.py`, and `_fn_block` / `_match_arm`
  from `tools/error_handling_check.py`. As of this session, four
  per-feature checkers share these parsers (`error_handling_check`,
  `connectivity_check`, `freshness_check`,
  `subscription_limit_check`). If a fifth ERR-* feature needs them
  (likely ERR-6 for the IB pacing budget port), strongly consider
  hoisting `_fn_block` / `_match_arm` / `_struct_body` / `_enum_body`
  / `_trait_body` into a shared helper module
  (e.g. `tools/_rust_parser.py`).
- The ExceededLimit-leaf message string contains the symbol and the
  strategy_id (e.g. `"AAPL"` and `"live-alpha-1"`). Both are
  operator-visible identifiers, not PII / secrets — the ERR-1 /
  ERR-2 / ERR-3 messages already include both, so this is consistent
  with the established pattern. The message also surfaces the
  configured limit value (e.g. `"100"`) which is operator-set
  configuration, not sensitive data.
- The judgment-pass `block` on commit 2 is a permanent feature of
  the gate, not a one-off. Any future change to `tools/critic_check.py`
  or `prompts/critic_prompt.md` will trip the same rule. The
  established procedure (split into two commits, AskUserQuestion
  sign-off, record the override in the commit message + progress.txt)
  is the workflow.

=== SESSION 15 ===
Date: 2026-05-11
Feature completed: ERR-3 — Market data stale: reject live order
submission with MARKET_DATA_STALE, publish a structured StaleDataEvent
carrying the observed staleness in seconds, do NOT request a reconnect
(staleness is a data-side condition, not a transport fault), and
produce zero IB order side effect (traces SRS-MD-004 + SyRS SYS-39a /
SYS-64 / SYS-87 / NFR-P5 15s threshold)
Status: 105 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub enum MarketDataFreshness { Fresh, Stale }` with a
    `const is_stale()` helper. `Stale` types the SRS-MD-004 /
    SyRS SYS-39a stale-data state.
  * Added `pub struct StaleDataEvent { state: MarketDataFreshness,
    strategy_id: StrategyId, symbol: String, staleness_seconds: u64 }`
    — exactly four fields, no broker / session / vendor / tick
    identifiers. The `staleness_seconds` scalar lets dashboards and
    the notification dispatcher surface how stale the feed actually
    got before the gate fired.
  * Added 3 new unit tests: `is_stale` coverage of the two states,
    `StaleDataEvent` exhaustive-destructure (proves no extra public
    fields exist), and an NFR-P5 above-15s sanity check. Total
    atp-types unit tests: 11 (was 8 in SESSION 14).
- Extended `crates/atp-execution/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait MarketDataFreshnessProbe { fn freshness(&self,
    symbol: &str) -> MarketDataFreshness; fn staleness_seconds(&self,
    symbol: &str) -> u64; }`. The port lives at the execution layer
    so the data-freshness gate is observable from execution without
    pulling `atp-execution` into a dependency on `atp-market-data`
    (SRS-ARCH-002). The eventual subscription-manager implementation
    will own the heartbeat timestamps, sequence-gap tracking, and
    the configurable threshold.
  * Added `pub trait StaleDataEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    StaleDataEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (later) route events to logs
    (SRS-LOG-001), the dashboard WebSocket, and the notification
    dispatcher.
  * Changed `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order` signature to take
    five port references: `broker: &B`, `connectivity: &C`,
    `events: &E`, `freshness: &F`, `stale_events: &S`. The
    `StrategyMode::Live` Connected sub-arm now nests a match on
    `freshness.freshness(&submission.symbol)`:
    `MarketDataFreshness::Fresh => broker.submit_order(submission)`
    is the happy path. `MarketDataFreshness::Stale =>` reads
    `staleness_seconds`, pushes a `StaleDataEvent` through
    `stale_events.record(...)`, then returns
    `Err(StructuredOrderError { category: MarketDataStale,
    error_type: "MarketDataStale", message: "...SRS-MD-004 + NFR-P5
    15s + observed Xs", original_order: submission })`. The broker
    port is NOT invoked on the Stale leaf, AND
    `connectivity.request_reconnect()` is NOT called (staleness is a
    data-side condition, not a transport fault).
  * Updated all 4 existing in-crate unit tests to thread
    `AlwaysFresh` (panics on `staleness_seconds`) / `ForbiddenFreshness`
    (panics on both methods) / `RecordingStaleEvents` (collects every
    recorded event) stubs through. Added 1 new unit test:
    `live_submission_is_blocked_when_market_data_is_stale` with a
    parameterized `StubFreshness` exercising the 22s staleness path.
    Total atp-execution unit tests: 7 (was 6 in SESSION 14).
- Updated `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_1_no_ib_side_effect.rs` to
  thread `AlwaysFresh` + `ForbiddenFreshness` + `StaleEventSinkSpy`
  stubs through the existing 3 ERR-1 tests. The Paper-mode
  ForbiddenFreshness stub proves Paper rejection still short-circuits
  before either the connectivity OR freshness gate is consulted. All
  3 tests pass under the new signature.
- Updated `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_2_connectivity_blocked.rs`
  to thread the new stubs through all 4 ERR-2 tests. The Unreachable
  / ScheduledRestartWindow tests use `ForbiddenFreshness` to prove
  the connectivity gate short-circuits ahead of the freshness gate
  (nested-match invariant). The Connected positive-control test now
  uses `AlwaysFresh`. All 4 tests still pass.
- Added `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_3_stale_data_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 4 tests):
  * `BrokerageSpy` (counts `submit_order`), `ConnectivitySpy`
    (parameterized state + counts reconnects), `EventSinkSpy`
    (connectivity events), `FreshnessSpy` (parameterized state +
    staleness_seconds + counts both probe methods), `ForbiddenFreshness`
    (panics on consultation), `StaleEventSinkSpy` (collects every
    recorded stale event).
  * `err_3_stale_state_blocks_live_submission_with_no_broker_call`
    — full ERR-3 contract: error category is `MarketDataStale`, wire
    string is `"MARKET_DATA_STALE"`, `broker.calls == 0`,
    `connectivity.reconnect_calls == 0` (data-side, not transport),
    `events.events.is_empty()` (no connectivity event), exactly one
    StaleDataEvent with `state == Stale`, `staleness_seconds == 22`,
    correct strategy/symbol, and freshness probe consulted exactly
    once with staleness_seconds probed exactly once.
  * `err_3_fresh_state_still_routes_through_broker` — negative
    control: Connected + Fresh reaches the broker (rejection is
    selective); freshness probe consulted once, staleness_seconds
    NOT probed (the Fresh leaf never asks for the age).
  * `err_3_unreachable_state_does_not_consult_freshness_port` —
    nested-match invariant: Unreachable + ForbiddenFreshness still
    rejects with CONNECTIVITY_BLOCKED (not MARKET_DATA_STALE),
    proving the ERR-2 connectivity gate short-circuits ahead of the
    ERR-3 freshness gate.
  * `err_3_stale_state_holds_across_many_live_submissions` —
    pseudo-property: sweeps 5 (strategy, symbol, qty, staleness)
    cases under Stale with staleness values [16, 30, 60, 999, 17]
    (NFR-P5 floor and well above); broker stays at 0, reconnect
    stays at 0, exactly 5 StaleDataEvents recorded with the correct
    per-case symbol and staleness_seconds.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **ERR-3b (deferred):** SRS-MD-004 requires the internal
  simulation engine to reject paper-on-sim submissions with
  `MARKET_DATA_STALE` too. The simulation engine in
  `crates/atp-simulation/src/lib.rs` is currently a stub with no
  submission entry point. The next sub-task should:
  (a) introduce `InternalSimulationEngine::submit_simulated_order`
      with a signature mirroring `submit_live_order` minus the
      brokerage port (no IB routing on the paper path);
  (b) wire the same `MarketDataFreshnessProbe` +
      `StaleDataEventSink` ports through it;
  (c) add a `crates/atp-simulation/tests/err_3b_sim_stale_data.rs`
      integration test paralleling
      `err_3_stale_data_blocked.rs`;
  (d) extend `tools/freshness_check.py` with an
      `assert_freshness_sim_static` peer of
      `assert_freshness_static`, and add a sim-side block to
      `architecture/runtime_services.json` (or extend the existing
      `freshness_contract` block with a `simulation_crate` /
      `sim_entry_point` field — recommend the latter to keep the
      single freshness gate as one logical contract);
  (e) flip ERR-3 retains `passes: true` for the live leg; ERR-3b
      is a fresh feature_list.json entry to be added if it does
      not already exist.
- The `submit_live_order` signature now takes five port references
  (broker, connectivity, connectivity events, freshness, stale
  events). Any future feature that adds a new guard (ERR-4
  line-limit, ERR-6 IB pacing, ERR-7 / ERR-8 liquidation timeouts)
  should follow the same pattern: introduce a port trait at the
  execution layer, extend the signature, and nest the new match
  inside the appropriate existing arm. ERR-4 (line-limit) and
  ERR-6 (pacing) most naturally nest inside Connected + Fresh.
  ERR-7 / ERR-8 (kill-switch / hot-swap liquidation timeouts) are
  not order-submission-path features and likely need a different
  entry point.
- The `error_type` field for the staleness rejection is
  `"MarketDataStale"` (CamelCase, like ERR-2's
  `"IbGatewayUnreachable"`). The SESSION 14 note about avoiding
  snake_case tokens inside core crates still applies:
  `market_data` could collide with the SRS-ARCH-002
  dependency-boundary regex if a future error_type uses it.
- `tools/freshness_check.py` reuses `_trait_body` from
  `tools/connectivity_check.py`. If a third ERR-* feature needs
  the same parser (likely ERR-6 for the IB pacing budget port),
  consider hoisting `_trait_body` into a shared helper module
  alongside `_fn_block` / `_match_arm` / `_struct_body` /
  `_enum_body`. Not urgent — there are only two callers today.
- The Stale-leaf message string contains the symbol (e.g. "AAPL").
  Symbols are operator-visible identifiers, not PII / secrets — the
  ERR-1 and ERR-2 messages already include the strategy ID, so this
  is consistent with the established pattern. If a future feature
  ever surfaces an order quantity in an error message, double-check
  it does not leak position-size information beyond the originating
  strategy.

=== SESSION 14 ===
Date: 2026-05-11
Feature completed: ERR-2 — IB Gateway unreachable: reject live order
submission with CONNECTIVITY_BLOCKED, publish a structured
ConnectivityEvent, attempt reconnection, and produce zero IB order side
effect (traces SRS-SAFE-003 + SRS-MD-005 + SyRS SYS-45 / SYS-46 / NFR-R2)
Status: 106 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub enum ConnectivityState { Connected, Unreachable,
    ScheduledRestartWindow }` with a `const is_blocked()` helper. The
    `Unreachable` variant types the SRS-SAFE-003 connectivity-loss
    state; `ScheduledRestartWindow` types the SRS-MD-005 daily-restart
    suspension state.
  * Added `pub struct ConnectivityEvent { state: ConnectivityState,
    strategy_id: StrategyId, symbol: String, scheduled_restart: bool }`
    — exactly four fields, no broker / session / vendor identifiers.
    The `scheduled_restart` flag is true iff the state is
    `ScheduledRestartWindow` so dashboards and the notification
    dispatcher can apply SRS-MD-005's suppression rule without
    re-inspecting the enum.
  * Added 3 new unit tests: `is_blocked` coverage of the three states,
    `ConnectivityEvent` exhaustive-destructure (proves no extra public
    fields exist), and the SRS-MD-005 suppression-flag round-trip.
- Extended `crates/atp-execution/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait BrokerageConnectivity { fn state(&self) ->
    ConnectivityState; fn request_reconnect(&self); }`. The port lives
    at the execution layer so the gate is observable from execution
    without pulling `atp-execution` into a dependency on
    `atp-adapters` (SRS-ARCH-002).
  * Added `pub trait ConnectivityEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    ConnectivityEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (later) route events to
    logs, the dashboard WebSocket (ALERTS / ACCOUNT_STATUS), and the
    notification dispatcher.
  * Changed `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order` signature to take
    three port references: `broker: &B`, `connectivity: &C`, `events:
    &E`. The `StrategyMode::Live` arm now nests a match on
    `connectivity.state()`. `ConnectivityState::Connected =>
    broker.submit_order(submission)` is the happy path.
    `Unreachable | ScheduledRestartWindow =>` builds a
    `ConnectivityEvent` (with the `scheduled_restart` flag computed
    via `matches!(state, ScheduledRestartWindow)`), pushes it through
    `events.record(...)`, calls `connectivity.request_reconnect()`,
    then returns `Err(StructuredOrderError { category:
    ConnectivityBlocked, error_type: "IbGatewayUnreachable",
    message: "...SRS-SAFE-003", original_order: submission })`. The
    broker port is NOT invoked on either blocked-state path.
  * Updated the 3 existing unit tests to thread always-connected /
    forbidden-connectivity stubs through. Added 2 new unit tests:
    `live_submission_is_blocked_when_gateway_unreachable` and
    `live_submission_is_blocked_during_scheduled_restart_window`. The
    Paper-mode test now uses `ForbiddenConnectivity` (panics on any
    call) to prove ERR-1's short-circuit is independent of the ERR-2
    connectivity gate.
- Updated `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_1_no_ib_side_effect.rs` to
  thread `AlwaysConnected` + `ForbiddenConnectivity` + `EventSinkSpy`
  stubs through the existing 3 tests. The ERR-1 contract is preserved:
  Paper submissions still reject with NON_LIVE_STRATEGY_SUBMISSION and
  zero broker side effect, and the Live control test still routes
  through. All 3 tests pass under the new signature.
- Added `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_2_connectivity_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 4 tests):
  * `BrokerageSpy` (counts `submit_order` calls), `ConnectivitySpy`
    (parameterized initial state + counts `request_reconnect`
    invocations), `EventSinkSpy` (collects every recorded event).
  * `err_2_unreachable_state_blocks_live_submission_with_no_broker_call`
    — full ERR-2 contract: error category is `ConnectivityBlocked`,
    wire string is `"CONNECTIVITY_BLOCKED"`, `broker.calls == 0`,
    `connectivity.reconnect_calls == 1`, exactly one event with
    `state == Unreachable` and `scheduled_restart == false`.
  * `err_2_scheduled_restart_window_blocks_with_suppressed_marker` —
    SRS-MD-005 path: same as above but with `state ==
    ScheduledRestartWindow` and `scheduled_restart == true`.
  * `err_2_connected_state_still_routes_through_broker` — negative
    control: Live + Connected reaches the broker (rejection is
    selective).
  * `err_2_unreachable_holds_across_many_live_submissions` —
    pseudo-property: sweeps 5 (strategy, symbol, qty) cases under
    Unreachable; broker spy stays at 0, reconnect spy hits exactly
    `cases.len()`, and exactly `cases.len()` events are recorded.
- Added `tests/domain/test_connectivity_blocked.py` (L7 Python domain
  test, 4 tests, marked `pytest.mark.domain` + `pytest.mark.safety`).
  Shells out to `cargo test -p atp-execution --test

  established `passes`-criterion for ERR-* features (ERR-1 SESSION 13
  set the precedent), the ERR-2 step list's final step explicitly
  accepts "side-effect absence" as evidence, and the SRS-SAFE-003
  verification method is "Fault injection" which the spy-driven
  Unreachable / ScheduledRestartWindow scenarios simulate. Production
  TCP probe / reconnect logic / dashboard fan-out / notification
  routing are tracked for later EXE-*, IB-adapter, NOTIF-1, and UI-*
  features in `architecture/README.md`'s deferred-work section. The
  second WARN (L7 test shells to cargo) likewise mirrors ERR-1's
  domain test pattern and is degradation-safe via `pytest.skip` when
  cargo is absent.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- ERR-2 lands the **connectivity safety gate** at the execution
  layer. There is still no production caller of
  `submit_live_order`; the orchestrator (later feature) will wire an
  `atp-adapters` `BrokerageAdapter` to `LiveBrokerageSubmit` and an
  IB-adapter probe to `BrokerageConnectivity` +
  `ConnectivityEventSink`. The gate is observable from execution
  without `atp-execution` depending on `atp-adapters`.
- The `submit_live_order` signature now takes three port references.
  Any future feature that adds a new guard (ERR-3 stale market data,
  ERR-4 line-limit, ERR-6 IB pacing, ERR-7 / ERR-8 liquidation
  timeouts) should follow the same pattern: introduce a port trait at
  the execution layer, extend the signature, and add the
  corresponding match arm inside the existing `StrategyMode::Live`
  branch. The progress.txt SESSION 13 note about "Each later ERR-*
  feature should add its own match arm" still applies.
- The `error_type` field for the connectivity rejection is
  `"IbGatewayUnreachable"` (CamelCase, distinct from the forbidden
  `ib_gateway` snake_case token that the SRS-ARCH-002 dependency
  boundary forbids inside core crates). The dependency check is
  case-sensitive substring, so `IbGateway` is safe; future ERR-*
  error_type strings should also stay in CamelCase to keep the
  dependency boundary regex green.
- `tools/connectivity_check.py` introduces a `_trait_body` helper
  that parses `pub trait <name> { ... }` bodies. If a third ERR-*
  feature needs to pin trait methods, the helper can be promoted to
  a shared module alongside `_enum_body` / `_struct_body` /
  `_fn_block` / `_match_arm`.
- Pre-existing dirty/untracked files unrelated to ERR-2:
  `.devserver.log`, `.devserver.pid`, `.claude/`, `.vscode/`,
  `prompts/coding_prompt.md`, `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`,
  `.critic_report.json` (the staged-diff JSON output of the
  deterministic critic — generated by this session, OK to keep or
  delete). They were not reverted.
- No features were skipped for clarification this session.
- Lowest remaining P1 by ID is ERR-3 (Market data stale), then
  ERR-4..ERR-9, then SRS-API-001 and beyond.

=== SESSION 13 ===
Date: 2026-05-11
Feature completed: ERR-1 — Order submitted by a non-live strategy to
live execution path: reject synchronously with structured error and
no IB order side effect (traces SRS-EXE-001 + SRS-ERR-001 + SyRS
SYS-1 / SYS-64 / AC-15)
Status: 107 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Moved `OrderSubmission` + `OrderReceipt` here from
    `atp-adapters` so both `atp-execution` (sender) and
    `atp-adapters` (impl side) share one definition without
    `atp-execution` depending on `atp-adapters` (dependency-direction
    rule: adapters and execution are siblings, both deps of types).
    Kept `pub use atp_types::{OrderReceipt, OrderSubmission}` in
    `atp-adapters` so existing callers compile unchanged.
  * Added `pub enum StrategyMode { Live, Paper }` with const
    `is_live()` — types the single-live-strategy designation
    (SRS-EXE-001 / SyRS AC-15).
  * Added `pub enum OrderErrorCategory` with 7 variants:
    `InvalidSymbol`, `InsufficientBuyingPower`,
    `ConnectivityBlocked`, `RateLimited`, `MarketDataStale`,
    `SubscriptionLimitReached`, `NonLiveStrategySubmission`. Each
    variant maps via `as_str()` to its SyRS SYS-64 upper-snake wire
    string (`"NON_LIVE_STRATEGY_SUBMISSION"` etc.) so the form is
    identical across Rust / Python / REST / WebSocket.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredOrderError { category, error_type,
    message, original_order }` — exactly the four fields
    SRS-ERR-001 requires, no broker/vendor identifier fields. Impl
    `Display` (renders `[CATEGORY] error_type: message`) + `Error`.
- Extended `crates/atp-execution/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait LiveBrokerageSubmit { fn submit_order(...) ->
    Result<OrderReceipt, StructuredOrderError>; }`. The port lives
    at the execution layer; adapters do not implement it directly —
    the orchestrator (later feature) wires an adapter to it. This
    keeps `atp-execution` free of any dep on `atp-adapters`.
  * Added `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order<B: LiveBrokerageSubmit>
    (&self, mode: StrategyMode, submission: OrderSubmission, broker:
    &B) -> Result<OrderReceipt, StructuredOrderError>` with a `match
    mode` whose `StrategyMode::Live` arm is the ONLY call site of
    `broker.submit_order(...)`. The `StrategyMode::Paper` arm
    returns `Err(StructuredOrderError { category:
    NonLiveStrategySubmission, error_type:
    "NonLiveLiveRouteBlocked", message: "strategy `{id}` is not the
    designated live strategy...SRS-EXE-001", original_order:
    submission })` BEFORE any broker call, so a Paper submission can
    never produce an IB order side effect.
  * Added 4 new unit tests in the same crate: routing happy path,
    paper-rejection with `broker.calls == 0` post-condition, the
    structured error display format, plus the existing boundary
    test was retained.
- Added `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_1_no_ib_side_effect.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 3 tests):
  * `BrokerageSpy` impls `LiveBrokerageSubmit` and increments a
    `Cell<u32>` on every call.
  * `err_1_paper_strategy_is_rejected_with_no_broker_call` —
    asserts the structured error has
    `category == NonLiveStrategySubmission`, the wire form is
    `"NON_LIVE_STRATEGY_SUBMISSION"`, `original_order` round-trips
    unchanged, and `spy.calls == 0`.
  * `err_1_holds_for_many_paper_submissions` — pseudo-property:
    sweeps 5 (strategy_id, symbol, qty) combinations including
    negative qty / zero qty / dotted ticker — spy stays at 0.
  * `err_1_live_strategy_still_routes_through_the_broker` —
    negative control: Live submissions DO reach the broker, so the
    rejection is selective and ERR-1 doesn't silently disable the
    live path.
- Added `tools/error_handling_check.py` (peer of
  `tools/historical_data_check.py`). 5 static checks + 1 cargo
  smoke:
  1. `atp-types` declares `StrategyMode` with `Live` + `Paper`.
  2. `atp-types` declares `OrderErrorCategory` with all 7 variants
     AND every SyRS SYS-64 wire string appears in the source (the
     `as_str()` arm encodes it).
  3. `atp-types` declares `StructuredOrderError` with the 4
     required fields and rejects the 4 forbidden vendor/broker
     fields (`broker`, `ib_order_id`, `vendor`, `provider`).
  4. `atp-execution` declares
     `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order` returning
     `Result<OrderReceipt, StructuredOrderError>`.
  5. Inside `submit_live_order`, `broker.submit_order(` appears
     ONLY inside the `StrategyMode::Live =>` match arm — not
     before the match, not inside the `StrategyMode::Paper =>`
     arm. The Paper arm must produce
     `OrderErrorCategory::NonLiveStrategySubmission`.
  6. `cargo test -p atp-execution --lib` + `--test
     err_1_no_ib_side_effect` smoke (skip on missing cargo).
  Reuses `_struct_body` / `_enum_body` from `historical_data_check`
  (no copy-paste). Exposes `assert_error_handling_static(config,
  root)` for the architecture-check short-circuit path.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- ERR-1 lands the **rejection vocabulary** only. The live IB
  routing pipeline (real submit, lifecycle state machine,
  correlation-ID idempotency, IB-pacing handling) lands with
  later EXE-* features. The brokerage port
  `LiveBrokerageSubmit` is defined at the execution layer; the
  orchestrator (later) wires an `atp-adapters` brokerage adapter
  to it. Right now no production code path constructs an impl
  of `LiveBrokerageSubmit` — only the test spy does. That is
  intentional: ERR-1's contract is "if such a port exists, a
  Paper submission can never invoke it."
- `OrderSubmission` and `OrderReceipt` now live in `atp-types`
  with a `pub use` re-export from `atp-adapters`. Any future
  feature that imports these types directly from
  `atp_adapters::` will keep working, but new code should
  prefer `atp_types::{OrderSubmission, OrderReceipt}` to make
  the dependency direction explicit.
- The structured-error vocabulary intentionally covers all 7
  SyRS SYS-64 categories (not just `NonLiveStrategySubmission`)
  so that ERR-2..ERR-9 can land without revisiting `atp-types`.
  Each later ERR-* feature should add its own match arm
  (mapping `AdapterError::*` → `OrderErrorCategory::*`) inside
  the corresponding execution-engine guard (connectivity,
  staleness, pacing, market-data-line limit, ingestion
  validation, hot-swap liquidation, kill-switch liquidation,
  startup config).
- `tools/error_handling_check.py` reuses `_struct_body` /
  `_enum_body` from `historical_data_check.py` (no copy-paste),
  matching the API-6 / API-7 import pattern. The check also
  introduces a `_fn_block` helper and a `_match_arm` helper
  that parses match arms with brace + string-literal awareness.
  Future ERR-* contract checks can promote these to a shared
  helper if more arms need pinning.
- The "no broker call outside Live arm" check is regex-based.
  A regression that hides the broker call behind a helper
  function call (e.g. `self.really_route(broker, submission)`)
  inside the Paper arm would pass the static check. The L7
  spy-adapter integration test is the runtime defense for this
  failure mode — the spy counts every call regardless of how
  it is reached.
- The `error_type` field in the Paper-arm error is
  `"NonLiveLiveRouteBlocked"`. If a later feature finds this
  string awkward, it can be renamed without touching the
  contract; only the *category* is part of the SRS-ERR-001
  wire vocabulary.
- Pre-existing dirty/untracked files unrelated to ERR-1:
  `.devserver.log`, `.devserver.pid`, `.claude/`, `.vscode/`,
  `prompts/coding_prompt.md`, `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`.
  They were not reverted (consistent with prior sessions).
- No features were skipped for clarification this session.
- Lowest remaining P1 by ID is ERR-2 (IB Gateway unreachable),
  then ERR-3..ERR-9 (stale market data, market-data line limit,
  ingestion validation, IB pacing, Hot-Swap liquidation timeout,
  kill-switch liquidation timeout, missing/invalid startup
  config), then SRS-API-001 and beyond.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- API-7 declares the unified historical query contract surface only —
  every `HistoricalDataAdapter::historical_data` call still returns
  `NotConfigured`. Real ingestion behaviour lands with DATA-1
  (Databento daily), DATA-2 (IB minute watchlist), DATA-3 (bulk
  backfill), DATA-4 (IB option-chain captures), DATA-5 (Sharadar
  fundamentals), DATA-6 (options DBN/Parquet), DATA-7 (unified
  historical access at runtime), and DATA-8..DATA-21 (cold reads,
  corporate actions, schema evolution).
- `HistoricalDataAdapter::historical_data` now returns
  `AdapterResult<HistoricalQueryResult>` instead of
  `AdapterResult<Vec<HistoricalBar>>`. This is a breaking change to
  the trait surface — downstream features that build on the trait
  must construct the envelope (symbol + asset_class +
  normalization_mode + bars) and not just bars.
- `tools/historical_data_check.py` reuses
  `tools/adapter_check.py::_trait_block` directly (no copy-paste),
  matching the API-6 import pattern. The new check tool also has its
  own `_struct_body` and `_enum_body` brace-matching helpers —
  future contract checks for new envelope-style result types
  (e.g. factor outputs) should consider promoting them to a shared
  helper.
- The Python protocol-method matcher in
  `tools/historical_data_check.py` deliberately skips single-line
  `def get_bars(...)` matches inside docstrings (doctest examples)
  by requiring a newline inside the parameter list. If a future
  refactor inlines the Protocol method onto a single line, the check
  will need to be relaxed.
- Pre-existing dirty/untracked files unrelated to API-7:
  `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`, `prompts/coding_prompt.md`,
  `Cargo.lock`, `requirements.txt`, `.claude/`, `.vscode/`. They were
  not reverted.
- No features were skipped for clarification.
- Lowest remaining P1 by ID is ERR-1 (system-error handling for an
  order submitted by a non-live strategy to live execution), then
  ERR-2..ERR-9 (IB Gateway unreachable, market data stale,
  market-data line limit exceeded, ingestion record validation
  failure, IB pacing budget exceeded, hot-swap demotion liquidation
  timeout, kill-switch liquidation timeout, missing/invalid startup
  configuration). These all trace to SRS-EXE / SRS-MD / SRS-DATA /
  SRS-ARCH error-handling clauses and are the natural next batch
  before the SRS-API-* / SRS-BT-* feature work.

=== SESSION 9 ===
Date: 2026-05-06
Feature completed: API-4 — operator CLI surface for kill switch,
strategy management, live designation, Hot-Swap, readiness status,
and basic administration (traces SRS-API-001 + SRS-SAFE-001)
Status: 111 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_cli/` that is the declarative
  source of truth for the operator CLI:
  * `commands.py` defines `Group` (6 buckets: kill-switch, strategy,
    live, hot-swap, readiness, admin), `ExitCode` (OK=0,
    USAGE_ERROR=2, CONFIRMATION_REQUIRED=3, NOT_FOUND=4, NOT_READY=5,
    TIMEOUT=6, NOT_IMPLEMENTED=64), frozen-slots `Argument` and
    `Command` dataclasses, the 18-entry `COMMANDS` tuple, and the
    access-policy constants `ACCESS_MODEL=local-shell`,
    `AUTH_MODEL=local-single-user`, `CLI_ENTRY_POINT=atp`. Each
    command carries `srs_refs`, `arguments`, `exit_codes`, and
    `requires_confirmation`. Four commands are confirmation-gated
    (kill-switch activate, strategy rollback, live promote,
    hot-swap trigger).
  * `manual.py` builds a deterministic JSON manual dict from
    `COMMANDS` (pure stdlib), with per-group `x-srs-refs`, per-command
    `x-srs-refs`/`x-requires-confirmation`, and document-level
    `x-access-model`/`x-auth-model` extensions encoding SRS-SEC-002.
  * `manual.json` is the frozen byte-equal snapshot.
  * `runner.py` builds an argparse parser from `COMMANDS`, exposes
    `python -m atp_cli --list` for surface introspection, enforces
    --confirm on irreversible commands (exit 3 on miss), and exits
    with NOT_IMPLEMENTED (64) for every stub handler.
  * `__main__.py` wires `python -m atp_cli`.
  * `__init__.py` re-exports the 17-name public surface.
  * `README.md` summarises access model, the 6-group/18-command
    table, exit codes, sample invocations, and snapshot regeneration.
- Added `tools/cli_check.py` mirroring `rest_api_check.py` and
  `websocket_api_check.py`: same exit-code contract, evidence-bullet
  output, `--update` flag. 11 checks total: 6 per-group (assert SRS
  refs, required commands, --confirm gating where applicable),
  `confirmation_invariant` (every irreversible command declares
  --confirm and CONFIRMATION_REQUIRED), `local_shell_policy`
  (constants + manual x-extensions), `exit_code_contract` (every
  command exit_codes ⊆ documented ExitCode and includes OK),
  `manual_snapshot` (byte-equality), `runner_smoke` (subprocess
  exercises --list, kill-switch activate without --confirm → exit 3,
  with --confirm → exit 64).
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json` with a `cli` block
  listing the 6 required groups, the manual snapshot path, the entry
  point, the access/auth policy, and the four confirmation-required
  commands. Extended `tools/architecture_check.py` with
  `assert_cli(config)` so the surface is enforced architecturally —
  `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` now adds an `atp_cli covers 6 groups and runs
  atp via local-shell (local-single-user)` evidence line.
- Wired `python3 tools/cli_check.py` into `init.sh` between the
  WebSocket API check and the deployment check; `✓ Environment ready`
  now requires the new check too.
- Added `tests/test_cli.py` (15 tests across 10 classes): subprocess
  contract test, command shape walk, group coverage (== set(Group),
  len 6, len(COMMANDS) == 18), confirmation invariant for the four
  irreversible commands, manual snapshot byte-equality, determinism,
  manual JSON parse, local-shell policy, exit-code contract, runner
  subprocess (list / confirm gating / NOT_IMPLEMENTED stub / readiness
  stub), parser build, commands_by_group, public-docstring walk.
- Tightened `tests/test_architecture.py` SRS-ARCH-001 aggregate test
  to require the new `atp_cli covers 6 groups` and `local-shell`
  evidence in the architecture-check output.
- Extended `architecture/README.md` with an `API-4` section
  documenting the direct check command, snapshot update recipe, and
  the parallel relationship to API-2/API-3.

What I tested (end-to-end, all 11 verifications):
1. `./init.sh` → `✓ Environment ready` with the new
   `→ Running CLI contract check…` line appearing between the
   WebSocket API step and the deployment-check step.
2. `python3 tools/cli_check.py` → `API-4 PASS` with 11 evidence

  RESV-1 (Hot-Swap), LOG-1 (logs), NOTIF-1 (alerts). `init.sh` still
  serves the placeholder `python3 -m http.server`.
- The CLI runner deliberately returns ExitCode.NOT_IMPLEMENTED (64)
  for every executable command. Downstream features should keep this
  exit code reserved for missing handlers and use the documented
  codes (OK, NOT_FOUND, NOT_READY, TIMEOUT, ...) for real outcomes.
- `requires_confirmation=True` commands MUST also document
  `ExitCode.CONFIRMATION_REQUIRED` and declare a `--confirm` argument
  with `required=True`. The check enforces all three at once; do not
  weaken any one of them without revisiting SRS-SAFE-001 / UI-4.
- No console-script entry point is wired today (no `pyproject.toml`
  scripts table). Operators invoke via `python -m atp_cli`. When a
  packaging step lands, set `[project.scripts] atp = "atp_cli.runner:main"`.
- `init.sh` is now stricter again: a broken `atp_cli` import or a
  missing manual snapshot fails init. Recover via
  `python3 tools/cli_check.py --update` or by running
  `python3 tools/cli_check.py` directly to see the failure.

  `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`, `prompts/coding_prompt.md`,

  not reverted.

  order submission, cancellation, account status, position queries —
  traces SRS-ARCH-003 and the BrokerageAdapter trait already present
  in `crates/atp-adapters`). The same declarative-contract pattern
  may not apply directly since adapter interfaces are Rust traits —
  consider surfacing them through a contract check that scans
  `crates/atp-adapters/src/` for the required trait methods.

=== SESSION 8 ===
Date: 2026-05-05
Feature completed: API-3 — WebSocket API contract surface for live
dashboard updates (P&L, metrics, account status, heartbeat, logs,
alerts, Reservoir ranking, strategy state)
Status: 112 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_ws/` that is the declarative
  source of truth for the operator WebSocket API:
  * `channels.py` defines `Direction`, `MessageType` (7 frames),
    `Channel` (8 buckets: PNL, METRICS, ACCOUNT_STATUS, HEARTBEAT,
    LOGS, ALERTS, RESERVOIR_RANKING, STRATEGY_STATE), frozen-slots
    `EventChannel` and `ClientCommand` dataclasses, the 8-entry
    `EVENT_CHANNELS` tuple, and the 3-entry `CLIENT_COMMANDS` tuple
    (SUBSCRIBE, UNSUBSCRIBE, HEARTBEAT_PING). `BIND_HOST=127.0.0.1`,
    `AUTH_MODEL=local-single-user`, `WS_PATH=/ws/v1`,
    `MAX_REFRESH_SECONDS=5` (NFR-P2 ceiling). Each channel carries
    `srs_refs`, `payload_fields`, `refresh_seconds` (0 means
    event-driven for LOGS/ALERTS), `requires_subscription`.
  * `asyncapi.py` builds a deterministic AsyncAPI 2.6 dict from
    EVENT_CHANNELS + CLIENT_COMMANDS (pure stdlib), with per-channel
    `subscribe` operations carrying `x-srs-refs`, `x-refresh-seconds`,
    `x-direction`, plus a multiplexed `/ws/v1/_control` channel for
    the SUBSCRIBE/UNSUBSCRIBE/HEARTBEAT_PING commands. Document-level
    `x-bind-host`/`x-auth-model`/`x-ws-path` extensions encode
    SRS-SEC-002.
  * `asyncapi.json` is the frozen byte-equal snapshot regenerated from
    `EVENT_CHANNELS`/`CLIENT_COMMANDS`.
  * `__init__.py` re-exports the 17-name public surface.
  * `README.md` summarises auth model, channel table with refresh
    cadence, message types, sample subscribe/event JSON, and snapshot
    regeneration recipe.
- Added `tools/websocket_api_check.py` mirroring `rest_api_check.py`:
  same exit-code contract, evidence-bullet output, `--update` flag.
  13 checks total: 8 per-channel (assert SRS refs, required payload
  fields, subscription required), `subscribe_protocol` (SUBSCRIBE +
  UNSUBSCRIBE both accept `channels` and reply ACK),
  `heartbeat_protocol` (HEARTBEAT_PING ↔ HEARTBEAT_PONG and traces
  SYS-39), `refresh_budget` (every channel within
  [0, MAX_REFRESH_SECONDS=5]s — NFR-P2), `asyncapi_snapshot`
  (byte-equality), `loopback_policy` (constants + x-extensions).
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json` with a `websocket_api`
  block listing 8 required channels, the AsyncAPI snapshot path,
  bind/auth/ws-path/refresh-ceiling policy. Extended
  `tools/architecture_check.py` with `assert_websocket_api(config)` so
  the surface is enforced architecturally — `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` now
  adds an `atp_ws covers 8 channels and binds 127.0.0.1 /ws/v1
  (local-single-user)` evidence line.
- Wired `python3 tools/websocket_api_check.py` into `init.sh` between
  the REST API check and the deployment check; `✓ Environment ready`
  now requires the new check too.
- Added `tests/test_websocket_api.py` (13 tests across 6 classes):
  subprocess contract test, EventChannel shape walk, channel
  coverage (== set(Channel), len 8), AsyncAPI snapshot byte-equality,
  determinism, AsyncAPI 2.6.0 parse, loopback policy, x-extensions,
  subscribe protocol, heartbeat protocol, NFR-P2 refresh budget,
  public-docstring walk.
- Tightened `tests/test_architecture.py` SRS-ARCH-001 aggregate test
  to require the new `atp_ws covers 8 channels` and `/ws/v1` evidence
  in the architecture-check output.
- Extended `architecture/README.md` with an `API-3` section
  documenting the direct check command, snapshot update recipe, and
  the parallel relationship to API-2 (`atp_api`).

What I tested (end-to-end, all 12 verifications from the plan):
1. `./init.sh` → `✓ Environment ready` with the new
   `→ Running WebSocket API contract check…` line appearing between

   STRATEGY_STATE` as expected.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- API-3 declares the contract only — no real WebSocket runtime exists
  yet. Concrete publishers (PNL/METRICS/HEARTBEAT/etc.) land with
  EXE-1, ORCH-1, MD-1, RESV-1, LOG-1, NOTIF-1. `init.sh` still serves
  the placeholder `python3 -m http.server`.
- Backtest-progress streaming is intentionally NOT a WebSocket channel.
  Backtest results are served by REST `GET /api/v1/backtests/{id}`
  (API-2). If a future feature needs streaming backtest progress,
  add a new `Channel.BACKTEST_PROGRESS` bucket and bump the snapshot.
- LOGS and ALERTS use `refresh_seconds=0` to mean *event-driven, no
  fixed cadence*. The check enforces the closed interval [0, 5]; do
  not tighten the lower bound to >0 without revisiting the contract.
- The control-plane (`/ws/v1/_control`) channel is a single AsyncAPI
  channel that carries a `oneOf` of three command messages
  (SUBSCRIBE/UNSUBSCRIBE/HEARTBEAT_PING). Per-command operationIds and
  response-message tags are encoded in `x-response-message`.
- `init.sh` is now stricter: a broken `atp_ws` import or a missing
  AsyncAPI snapshot fails init. Recover via
  `python3 tools/websocket_api_check.py --update` or by running
  `python3 tools/websocket_api_check.py` directly to see the failure.
- Pre-existing dirty/untracked files unrelated to API-3:
  `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`, `prompts/coding_prompt.md`,
  `Cargo.lock`, `requirements.txt`, `.claude/`. They were not
  reverted.
- No features were skipped for clarification.

  strategy management, live designation, Hot-Swap, readiness, basic
  admin — traces SRS-API-001 + SRS-SAFE-001). The same
  declarative-contract pattern (channels module + introspection
  check + frozen snapshot + architecture wiring) should apply.

=== SESSION 7 ===
Date: 2026-05-05
Feature completed: SRS-ARCH-005 - Configuration system for credentials,
storage paths, IB account settings, market-data line limits, resource
limits, and notification channels
Status: 113 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a top-level `configuration` block to
  `architecture/runtime_services.json` cataloguing 16 required keys
  across the six SRS-ARCH-005 categories (credentials, storage_paths,
  ib_account, market_data_limits, resource_limits, notification_channels).
  Each key carries name, category, type (int|float|path|secret|enum|host),
  validator hints (min/max, non_empty, absolute, choices), default,
  secret flag, and SRS trace.
- Added five new resource-limit env vars to close the SyRS SYS-57/58
  gap that previously lived only as static compose labels:
  ATP_LIVE_STRATEGY_MEM_MB=512, ATP_LIVE_STRATEGY_CPU=0.25,
  ATP_PAPER_STRATEGY_MEM_MB=300, ATP_PAPER_STRATEGY_CPU=0.10,
  ATP_HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB=2048. They are threaded through
  `.env.example`, `init.sh` defaults, the `x-atp-env` anchor in
  `docker-compose.yml`, and the existing
  `deployment.required_env_vars` list (which deployment_check.py now
  validates at the compose layer).
  IMPORTANT: the env vars are deliberately NOT substituted into the
  strategy-runtime service's `deploy.resources.limits` block. Compose's
  `memory:` field requires a unit suffix (e.g. `512M`); a raw integer
  silently means *bytes* and would OOM at boot. The compose block
  remains the static template default; the orchestrator (SRS-ORCH-002,
  future feature) reads the env vars at per-strategy clone time.
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_config/` (pure stdlib):
  * `schema.py` — `Category`, `KeyType`, `Severity` enums; `KeySpec`
    and `ReadinessFailure` dataclasses; `ReadinessReport` with `ok`,
    `errors`, `warnings`, `as_json_lines()`. `REQUIRED_KEYS` is loaded
    from runtime_services.json at import time so the JSON catalogue is
    the single source of truth.
  * `validate.py` — `load_and_validate(env, *, atp_env=None)` returning
    a structured `ReadinessReport`. Per-type validators: int/float
    parse + range; path non-empty + absolute; host non-empty;
    secret non-empty; enum choices. Production-mode escalation: a
    placeholder secret is a *warning* in development and a hard *error*
    when ATP_ENV is staging/production, so init.sh dev defaults still
    pass while staging/production cannot start with placeholders.
  * `__init__.py` re-exports the public surface (15 names).
  * `README.md` documents the categories, every key, validation rules,
    and the readiness-failure JSON-line shape (covers the
    "documented" half of the SRS-ARCH-005 AC).
- Added `tools/config_check.py` mirroring the
  `tools/deployment_check.py` pattern: same exit-code contract,
  evidence-bullet output, --fixture flag (modes:
  `missing-credential`, `placeholder-secret-in-production`,
  `invalid-line-limit`, `missing-resource-limit`,
  `invalid-storage-path`), and an `assert_configuration_static()`
  aggregator entry that `tools/architecture_check.py` consumes.
- Wired `assert_configuration_static` into `tools/architecture_check.py`
  after the SRS-ARCH-004 deployment evidence, so the aggregate
  `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` output now ends with a
  `SRS-ARCH-005 configuration system evidence:` bullet group with one
  line per category.
- Wired `python3 tools/config_check.py` into `init.sh` after the
  deployment-check step. `✓ Environment ready` now requires the
  configuration check to pass.
- Added `tests/test_configuration.py` (24 tests): catalogue shape,
  validator behaviour for every type, structured-failure shape,
  JSON round-trip, public-docstring walk, placeholder constant
  matches `.env.example`.
- Added 5 cases to `tests/test_architecture.py`
  (positive + 4 negative fixtures) and tightened the SRS-ARCH-001
  assertion to require the SRS-ARCH-005 evidence header.
- Extended `docs/DEPLOYMENT.md` with a `## Configuration system
  (SRS-ARCH-005)` section listing all 16 keys by category, the
  validation rules, the structured failure schema, the
  staging/production placeholder-escalation rule, and the explicit
  note that compose-substitution into deploy.resources.limits is
  deliberately avoided. Added an `SRS-ARCH-005` section to
  `architecture/README.md` with the direct check command and the
  five negative fixtures.

What I tested (end-to-end, all 12 verifications from the plan):

    SRS-MD-006, not SRS-ARCH-005. The MD-006 implementation should
    consume the same `configuration.keys` JSON catalogue from
    runtime_services.json and re-validate at orchestrator boot.
  * The orchestrator is the eventual enforcement point for the new
    resource-limit env vars (SRS-ORCH-002). The compose
    strategy-runtime `deploy.resources.limits` block remains the
    template default; do NOT change it to substitute from the env
    vars without also normalising the values into compose's required
    unit-suffixed format.

  catalogue key fails init. Revert by setting the missing key in env

=== SESSION 3 ===
Date: 2026-05-03
Feature completed: API-2 - REST API contract surface for SRS-API-001
Status: 117 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_api/` that is the declarative source of truth for
  the operator REST API:
  * `routes.py` defines `Method`, `Capability` (11 buckets), and a `Route` dataclass with
    SRS-traced fields. The 14-route `ROUTES` tuple covers every API-2 capability
    (lifecycle, live designation, kill switch, Hot-Swap, backtest launch/query,
    Reservoir ranking, watchlist config, system status, logs, alerts).
  * `openapi.py` builds a deterministic OpenAPI 3.1 dict from `ROUTES` (pure stdlib).
  * `openapi.json` is the frozen byte-equal snapshot regenerated from `ROUTES`.
  * `BIND_HOST=127.0.0.1` and `AUTH_MODEL=local-single-user` encode the SRS-SEC-002
    loopback policy ("Local single-user deployment controls").
  * `README.md` summarises auth model, capability table, confirmation routes, sample
    curl, and the snapshot regeneration recipe.
- Added `tools/rest_api_check.py` — mirror of `strategy_api_check.py`. Prints "API-2 PASS"
  with 13 evidence bullets (one per capability + snapshot freshness + loopback policy).
  Supports `--update` to rewrite the OpenAPI snapshot from current `ROUTES`.
- Added `tests/test_rest_api.py`: subprocess contract test, route shape walk, capability
  coverage (== set(Capability)), OpenAPI snapshot byte-equality, snapshot determinism,
  loopback policy, kill-switch + live-designation confirmation guards, public docstrings.
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json` with a `rest_api` block listing the 11
  required capabilities, the snapshot path, and the loopback/auth policy. Extended
  `tools/architecture_check.py` with `assert_rest_api(config)` so the surface is
  enforced architecturally — `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` now adds an `atp_api covers 11
  capabilities and binds 127.0.0.1` evidence line.
- Extended `init.sh` to run `python3 tools/rest_api_check.py` after the static-server
  smoke test; `✓ Environment ready` now requires both checks to pass. Cargo-tolerance
  preserved.
- Routes that perform irreversible actions (POST /api/v1/kill-switch, POST
  /api/v1/strategies/{id}/promote-live) carry `requires_confirmation=True` and a
  `confirm` query parameter, traced to SRS-SAFE-001 and SYS-2d respectively.

What I tested (end-to-end, all six verifications):
1. `./init.sh` -> "✓ Environment ready" with both smoke test and "Running REST API
   contract check..." steps shown.
2. `python3 tools/architecture_check.py` -> "SRS-ARCH-001 PASS" with the new rest_api
   evidence line.
3. `python3 tools/rest_api_check.py` -> "API-2 PASS" with 13 evidence bullets (11
   capabilities + snapshot in-sync + loopback policy).
4. `python3 -m unittest tests.test_architecture tests.test_strategy_api
   tests.test_rest_api` -> 21 tests OK.
5. Snapshot determinism: regenerate `render_snapshot()` -> byte-equal (30,006 bytes)
   to `python/atp_api/openapi.json`.
6. Deterministic re-run of the contract script -> identical PASS output.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- `init.sh` is now stricter. A broken `atp_api` import fails init (intended; matches
  the API-1 precedent of architecture_check failing fast). If a future change to
  `ROUTES` is unintended, `tools/rest_api_check.py --update` regenerates the snapshot.
- Hot-Swap automatic-trigger configuration (drawdown threshold, top-rank/momentum
  enable, 7-day cool-down policy edits) is server-internal in this contract; only
  manual promotion (`POST /api/v1/hot-swap`) and `GET /api/v1/hot-swap/status` are
  REST-exposed. A future feature can add `PUT /api/v1/hot-swap/policy` if needed.
- Confirmation is modeled as a `confirm` query parameter on the route declaration; the
  two-step UX (modal + token) lands with UI-4 / dashboard work.
- API-2 declares the contract only — no real HTTP runtime exists yet. `init.sh` still
  serves the placeholder `python3 -m http.server`. Live handlers come with EXE-1,
  ORCH-1, RESV-1, BT-1, DATA-1, LOG-1, NOTIF-1.
- WebSocket overlap deliberately avoided: API-3 owns `/ws/*`. Re-confirm before adding
  any streaming routes here.
- `architecture/container_manifests.json` is still missing (pre-existing); recommend a
  small architecture-cleanup feature to either remove the reference from
  `architecture_check.py` or commit the file.
- Lowest remaining P1 by ID is API-3 (WebSocket API surface) — same contract-evidence
  pattern should apply: declarative event schema + introspection check + snapshot.

Feature completed: API-1 - Python Strategy API contract for SRS-SDK-001..009

What I did:
- Extended `python/atp_strategy/api.py` with the full Strategy API surface required by API-1's
  description: AssetClass, StrategyConfig (with warmup_bars and tradable_asset_class),
  OrderEventType, OrderEvent (with fill_price/fill_quantity/commission/order ids), Scheduler

  StrategyContext with cancel/indicator/consolidate and the asset_class kwarg on subscribe,
  and added on_warmup_complete/on_schedule callbacks plus a warmup_bars class attr to Strategy.
- Added `python/atp_strategy/indicators.py` with pure-Python incremental SMA, EMA, RSI, MACD,
  BollingerBands, ATR — all implementing the Indicator Protocol with no external deps.
- Wrote `python/atp_strategy/README.md` author guide with runnable Example sections covering
  every capability bucket (SRS-SDK-009).
- Added `tools/strategy_api_check.py` contract evidence script that prints API-1 PASS with one
  bullet per SDK-001..009, mirroring the SRS-ARCH-001 pattern.
- Added `tests/test_strategy_api.py`: subprocess contract test, protocol shape test,
  indicator incremental update test, asset-class violation test, public-docstrings walk,
  and Strategy base-class smoke tests.
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json` required_exports to 29 names so the existing
  `tools/architecture_check.py` enforces the new surface architecturally without code changes.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- The pure-Python indicator implementations satisfy the SRS-SDK-006 incremental-update
  acceptance criterion, but numerical parity with pandas-ta / TA-Lib reference outputs is
  deferred to a sibling feature (suggest INDICATOR-1) — those deps are not in scope yet.
- StaticTradingCalendar is a minimal NYSE-shaped weekday-only calendar (no holidays, no DST).
  Full holiday/DST coverage for SRS-SDK-002 is deferred to a sibling feature (suggest CAL-1)
  with `exchange_calendars` or equivalent.
- SRS-SDK-007 (P2) and SRS-SDK-008 (P3) are exposed as Protocols only; concrete
  bar-consolidation and Renko/range-bar implementations come with later features.
- Live-vs-paper driver equivalence (SRS-SDK-001 acceptance) is contract-asserted here (no
  execution-mode parameters leak into StrategyContext); the actual driver-equivalence test
  belongs to EXE-1/SIM-1 once those engines exist.
- Backwards-incompatible change: Strategy.on_order_event now takes an OrderEvent (was
  OrderHandle). No existing strategy authors yet, so the break is accepted.
- Lowest remaining P1 by ID is API-2 (REST API surface).
